Business News, Finance

Gold Price Rises by 9.3 Taels

Slight Fluctuations, Yesterday the 17th, the Gold Price Soared, Meng Jin Only had Minor Changes, with Slight Advances and Retreats. The Overall Market Even had a Review of 17 Taels. As a Result, it Soared by 9 Taels and Several Points. Almost Never had the Silver Market seen a Rise or Fall. People's Hearts Initially felt Weak, Leading to a Drop at the Opening. Unexpectedly, Major Players Covered their Short Positions, Especially due to a Certain Bank's Aggressive Purchases, which were Significant. In Addition, Various Firms Followed Suit, Competing to Purchase. The Buying Sentiment in the Market was Pervasive, and Due to the Tension in Exchange Rates, the Market Trend Continued to Rise. It Advanced Courageously and Soared by more than 10 Taels, Actually Exceeding the 790 Taels Mark, with Only a Minor Retracement of 3 or 4 Taels. The Subsequent Market Slightly Weakened as the Foreign Exchange Rate Stabilized, and the Buying Momentum Began to Subside. Multiple Parties seemed to be Unloading, but the Situation was Peaceful, Remaining Within 90 Taels. It is Said that There may not be Major Changes in Large Bars of Silver, and a Slight Decrease is Expected.

From Low to High, the October Opening Price in the Morning Decreased by 3.5 Taels to 775 Taels. This was because the Decline in Large Bars had not been Completed Last Weekend. Subsequently, Yuan Xing, Yong Qian, Chang Xiang, Da Xing, Yong Yuan Mao, Yong Chang Sheng, Yong Shun Mao, etc., Successively Pushed Forward. It was Heard that a Certain Bank was Engaged in Absorption, and Speculators and Various Firms followed Suit, Leading the Short Sellers to Forcefully Cover and the Long Positions to Increase. Also, the British Gold Closed at Only 4375 to Half a Penny. Hua Bank Absorbed 5625 to Half a Penny. In an Instant, the Situation Changed Rapidly, and it Rose Gradually by 7 Taels, with Only a Fluctuation of 1 Tael. Until the British Gold was Listed, it did not Change, Standing at 82 Taels and 2 Mace, Deducting About 6 or 7 Mace. Sanjing Absorbed October Half a Penny, and also Offered November Prices at the Same Rate. This was a Swap. Before Long, HSBC Offered September at 4375, and Yuan Xing, Yong Qian, Chang Xiang, etc., Continued to Purchase, Immediately Jumping Up 7 Taels. At 9:45, it Reached 89 Taels. After Entering, Nei Xing, Shunli, Wan Xing, etc., Took Advantage of this to Unload, and Because Fellow Traders Re-Sold British Gold, it Retreated by More Than 3 Taels. Approaching 10 O'Clock, it was 85 Taels and 67 Cents. However, the Bank Bought British Gold at Half a Penny and also Absorbed Citibank at 29 Yuan and 4375, and Major Players Competed to Purchase Again and Again. At 10:10, it had Reached 90 Taels and Soon Reached 91 Taels. Afterwards, Sellers Seemed to be More Numerous, so it Moved Downstream. However, with Sudden Advances and Retreats, there were More Than 3 Taels of Circling. The Exchange Market Stabilized and did not Change Significantly. Until 11 O'Clock, it was 87 Taels 1 or 2 Cents. Soon after, Gan Chang Xiang, Yuan Xing, Yong Yu, Da Yuan Tai, Fu Tai Heng, etc., All Made Purchases, so it Increased by 3 or 4 Taels. After 11:30, the Indian Exchange Rate was Near Small and Far Large, but Only Two Annas. The Gold Price had Already Risen to 91 Taels. In a Moment, it Retraced 2 Taels, Reaching 89 Taels, Because Retail Investors and the Dalian Group Sold. However, the Long Positions Forcefully Pulled it Up, and in Just 7 or 8 Minutes, it Soared to 92 Taels. Unexpectedly, British Gold could be Settled at 4375 in the Near Term and Half a Penny in the Far Term, so the Noon Closing was 90 Taels. Subsequently, the Situation was Flat, and Goods were also Collected at 90 Taels. The Closing Price was Still 819 Taels, Estimated at a Pressure of 367 or 8 Taels to 27 or 8 Taels.

Peaceful Situation, the Subsequent Market Opened at 88 Taels and 8 Mace. People's Hearts were Calm. Suddenly, it was Heard that the Indian Exchange Rate Reported Small at 2 or 3 Annas, Immediately Rising to 90 Taels and 05 Cents. In a Moment, Yuan Chun Lai Sold, and it Retraced to 88 Taels and a Half. Immediately, it Rose Again to 89 Taels and 6 Mace, Because Sanjing Bought November British Gold at Half a Penny. Afterwards, it seemed to Turn Downward. The Cover Selling, Tong Huo Heng, and Others Unloaded. The Dalian Group's Supply Exceeded Demand. At 3:10, it was 87 Taels and 8 Mace. Soon After, Ri Chang, Gan Chang Xiang, Da Cheng, Yong Heng, etc., Came to Buy, and Sumitomo Absorbed November at 1 or 2 Half, Rising Again by More Than 2 Taels. At 3:30, it was 90 Taels and 04 Cents. Helplessly, Yuan Xing, Yong Zhi Feng, Yong Jin An, etc., Re-Sold, Causing the Price to Fail to Advance, and it Retraced 3 Taels. After 4 O'Clock, it Re-Entered 90 Taels. Afterwards, it was Only 87 Taels and 1 Mace. By the Time the Market Closed at 4:30, it was 87 Taels and 8 Mace. Subsequently, it Decreased Again to Within 7 Taels, with Scattered Long Positions Unloading. Seeing that the Silver Market Failed to Contract, it was Comparatively Higher Than Last Saturday (According to the Listing Price) by 9 Taels and 3 Mace. According to the Daily Maximum of 92 Taels and Minimum of 75 Taels, there were Fluctuations of 17 Taels.

Spot Silver, Delivery Flat, Goods Early Market 74 Taels and 1 Mace, Noon Closing 90 Taels, Afternoon 89 Taels and 8 Mace, Closing Price 87 Taels, Listed Price Estimated at a Pressure of 30 Taels, Registered at 87 Taels to 90 Taels, Water Supplement 87 Taels, Afternoon 85 Taels, Spot Silver Bars Initially had no Transactions. Soon After, Ying Feng Heng Absorbed 7 or 8 Hundred Taels, Sold by Fellow Traders, Estimated at an Addition of 8 Taels. Afterwards, the Firm Sold it to Tianjin Dalian, Carrying 4 or 5 Thousand Taels, Estimated at an Addition of 9 Taels. Other Spot Firms also Sold.

Speculation was Lively, and Transactions on the Table were Quite Active. According to Statistics, Yuan Xing Yong, Gan Chang Xiang, Da Xing Yong Altogether Bought Ten Thousand Several Thousand Bars, Acting on Behalf of a Certain Bank. Yuan Mao Yong's Inflow and Outflow was Quite Frequent. Wu Covered his Short Positions Quite a Bit. Shun Mao, Yuan Heng, and Chang Sheng Yong Immediately Entered Early On. Fu Tai Heng, Cui Chang Yong, and Cheng Feng Yong All Entered. Tong Tai Chang and Yi Feng Yong Entered More and Exited Less. Wan Xing, Shunli, Tong Feng Heng, and Bing Xing Mostly Sold. Yuan Tai, Sen Chang Yong, Yuan Chun, Zhi Feng Yong, and Da De Cheng had a Large Inflow and Outflow. In the Afternoon, Zhi Feng Yong and Yuan Feng Yong Entered and then Exited. Shunli, Wan Xing, Cui Chang Yong, and Jin An All Exited. Yong Heng, Ri Chang, Gan Chang Xiang, Fu Tai Heng, and Da De Cheng All Entered. Yuan Tai, Tong Tai Chang, Yuan Mao Yong, Goods, and Yong De Yi Feng Yong Sometimes Entered and Sometimes Exited. The Dalian Group Altogether Sold One Thousand Four or Five Hundred Bars, Altogether Exiting Four Thousand Five or Six Hundred Bars. The Guangdong Group Still had No Action. London Large Bars Still Remained Unchanged.

The National Society's London Dispatch on the 17th: Today's London Silver Price Closed with the Near and Far Term Both Remaining at 12 Pence 625. The Foreign Exchange Rate was Initially Flat and then Tight.

Yesterday HSBC's Listing Price Remained Unchanged. This was Because the British and American Silver Markets had No Rise or Fall the Day Before. The Bank's Internal Market was Initially Flat and then Tight. In the Afternoon, it Stabilized. However, the Market Situation was Not as Aggressive as the Gold Market. It had Already Broken Through the 790 Taels Barrier. This was Actually Because a Bank Made Large-Scale Purchases and Major Players Covered Their Short Positions, Arousing People's Hearts. As a Result, Compared to Last Saturday, the British Gold Slightly Contracted by 0.0625, the American Gold by 1.25, and the Japanese Gold Added 1 Cent. Commercial Transactions were Very Active. Generally, Demand Exceeded Supply. It was Estimated that About 300,000 Pounds of British Gold were Transacted, with HSBC Selling Positions and Sanjing Having a Not Small Appetite. It was Heard that there were Still Quite a Few Imports for Settlement by Foreign Firms During the Day. Also, the American Gold did not Exceed 140,000 Yuan, and the Japanese Gold Settled for More than 1 Million Yuan. Sanjing had a Strong Desire to Buy.

British Exchange Internal Market Estimated at a Fluctuation of 0.0625. The Morning Price was Recently 1 Shilling 2 and a Half Pence to 5625. The Long-Term was 5625 to 625. The Purchase Price was Increased by 0.0625. Sanjing and Holland did Business for October at 5625. The Wheat Firm Offered 90 Months at 4375. HSBC Offered September Half a Penny. Sanjing Entered October and Offered November at the Same Price, Half a Penny. HSBC and Sanjing Offered 90 Months at 4375 and also 4375 to Half a Penny. Sanjing, Sumitomo, and Hefeng Entered October Half a Penny. Shanghai Hefeng and Sanjing Offered November at the Same as Above. Sumitomo Hui Offered November at the Same as Above. Pan Yin Offered September at 4375. The Noon Closing Price was Offered at 4375 to Half a Penny. In the Afternoon, Sanjing Such as Sumitomo Bought October and November Half a Penny. The Closing Price was Offered at 4375 to Half a Penny. The Purchase Price was Half a Penny to 5625.

The Purchase Price was Increased by 1.25. The Wheat Firm Offered 90 Months at 4375. Sanjing Entered at 375 and also Hui December at 4375. The Mainland Offered and Sanjing Entered Mutual Business November 375. The Noon Closing Price was Offered at 1875 to 3125. The Afternoon Closing Price was the Same.

Development of Cotton Yarn Market

The Yarn Market was Tighter Because the Overseas Market was Stable, and the Current Yarn Sales were More Successful. Sichuan Merchants Acted Actively Because a Major Flood Occurred in Hankou, and Two Yarn Factories there were Flooded and Unable to Work, so the Sichuan Merchants Purchased in Shanghai. However, the Yunnan Merchants' Appetite was Satiated and there were No Transactions. As a Result, People's Hearts were High. Currently, There is a Real Need, and There is a Possibility of a Rise. However, Major Players Still Sell on Rises.

The Human Biao Rose by 1 Tael. The Foreigners' Biao the Previous Market Opening saw a Slight Rise in American Cotton and the Gold Price was Good, Leading to Tighter People's Hearts. Each Month Rose by 1 Tael 1.2 Qian to 1 Tael 8 Qian. In the Afternoon, it was Heard that the Real Need was Smooth, and the Market Situation was Still Good. The Near Term Fell by 3.5 Qian and the Far Term Rose by 3.4 Qian. Transactions were Estimated at 45,000 Bales. Buying was Inspected at Gong Tai 700 Bales, Tong Yu 500 Bales, Geng Feng 5350 Bales, Yi Yu 1450 Bales, Xin Cheng 1000 Bales, Xie Sheng Da Chang 1100 Bales, Heng De 800 Bales. Buying was Inspected at Gu Feng 2100 Bales, Yong Feng 1100 Bales, Chang Feng 4600 Bales. The Closing Prices are Recorded on the Left.

Cotton Market was Sharp

The Cotton Market was Tighter and Rising Because the Gold Price was Soaring Again and Foreign Cotton Also Rose Slightly, Leading to Good People's Hearts. Also, There were More New Long Positions. Because the Decline in American Cotton had Stabilized and the Hankou Flood was Still Severe, the Situation was More Tense. However, Some Manufacturers, Because the World Cotton Industry was in Surplus and American and Indian Cotton Prices were Cheaper, Still Cashed Out Biao Cotton. The Cotton Market Situation Still Needs to Follow American Cotton for Advances and Retreats.

Han Biao Rose by 4 or 5 Qian. The Han Biao Previous Market Opening saw a Slight Rise in the American and Indian Cotton Markets, and the Atmosphere was Tighter. Also, Major Players Made Purchases. Each Month Rose by 3, 4 or 5 Qian. In the Afternoon, it Rose Another 1 Qian. Transactions were Estimated at 84,60,000 Dan. Buying was Inspected at Tong Yu 2,100 Dan, Zhen Da 1,900 Dan, Xie Sheng 2,100 Dan, Yong Feng 1,200 Dan, Da Ji 2,100 Dan, Da Chang 1,700 Dan. Indian and British Cotton Industry Weekly News

Mumbai's Market Situation Last Week was Firm and Stable, Not Plunging with the American Cotton Government Report. The American and Indian Price Ratio on Monday was Too High, with Only a Difference of 25 Pounds Yin. This was Because the Two Markets Rose and Fell Differently. Once it is Balanced, it Must Return. The Current Need is Dim and Export Demand is Lacking Because the Price Ratio is Higher, and No One is Willing to Buy Indian Cotton. European Inquiries are Not Good. An Appendix to Last Week's Statistics is as Follows (Unit: Thousands of Bales).

Liverpool's Spot Sales Improved Slightly Last Week. In Terms of Futures, After the American Government Report was Released, Market Prices Plunged Sharply. However, the Sales Volume was Absorbed by Fellow Traders. Mainland Manufacturers Advanced Sharply on the Dips, so it Gradually Returned. Afterwards, the Department of Agriculture's Destruction Plan was Opposed, and the Market Situation was Unstable Again. Egyptian Cotton Transactions were Very Good, and Prices Rose and Fell with American Cotton.

Grain

River Down Rice Market Arrivals and Sales were Balanced.

The Origin of Various Merchants in the Southern Market Continued to Connect. It was Argued that the Market Sentiment Changed from Weak to Flat. Buyers' Intention to Enter was Due to the Continuation of Arrivals. Moreover, Stockpilers did not Relax, Leading to Scanty Sales. The Decline in Thick Japonica and Thin Indica Rice Stabilized. More Than 1,000 Stones of Dongxin Japonica Rice from the North and South Markets were Available. Scattered Sales were Scarce. Prices did not Rise or Fall. There was Not Much High-Quality Water-Grown Pointed Rice. Middle Grades were Crowded by Buyers, and the Market Seemed Slow, Leading to Price Cuts. Arrivals and Sales of Yin Hua Rice were Balanced, and the Market did not Rise or Fall.

Zhabei's Inland Arrivals were Limited. The Top Grade of Northern Japonica Rice was Scarce, and Movement Reached Nearly 1,000 Stones. The Market Price for Top Grades was Stable, and Middle and Low Grades Decreased by 4 Jiao. The Arrivals of Green 角, Indica Rice, and Jin Lu were Few. However, the Appetite was Limited, and the Situation was Weak. Water-Grown Pointed Rice was the Same. It was Argued that Pointed Rice was Scarce and there was No Market. Glutinous Rice was Not Prosperous or Humiliated. Although the Passages of Foreign Rice by Merchant Groups and the Main Street were Sparse, Buyers Showed Strength Because Stockpiles were Thin. Foreign Rice Sales were Sluggish and Decreasing.

Yesterday's Foreign Rice Market Situation in the Morning, Local Buyers Lacked Inflow and Outflow. The Market was Very Weak. Cargo Owners Desiring to Sell Quickly were Willing to Sell at Discounted Prices. The Situation was Even More Sluggish. Prices had a Potential to Decrease by 1 or 2 Jiao. Scattered Households and Stockpilers on the Main Street Took Advantage of Small Purchases. The Market Turned to Flat. A Total of More Than 1,000 Packages of Annam were Opened, Accounting for More Than Half. This was Because the Community Japonica Rice Price Plate was Higher. The Main Street Needed to Piece Together, so the Prices Opened at 15 Yuan, 14 Yuan 8 or 9 Jiao, and Subsequently 14 Yuan 5 or 6 Jiao. Yu Dang Rice was Only 400 Packages, and the Price was 13 Yuan 4 Jiao. It was Said that the Biao Flour's Subsequent Market Showed a Slight Decline.

Yesterday's Flour Market, After the Market Opened in the Morning, Various Months' Markets Saw Slight Improvement in the Foreign Wheat Quotation of 1 or 2 Jiao. In Addition, the Gold Price was Tense, so the Near and Far Term People's Hearts were Quite Firm (The Southeast Asian Merchants Also Moved Slightly). The Buying Momentum of Inland Merchants was Still Rushing. The Closing Prices for Various Months were Generally Better Than the Previous Week by About 1 Fen. Until the Market Opened in the Afternoon, the Market Sentiment Returned to Softness. The Wheat Market was Weak, and it was Rumored that Foreign Wheat, Which was Planned to Advance, Would be Sold to Chinese Merchants at a Low Price, so People's Hearts Suddenly Softened. Both the Near and Far Term Showed Laxity. However, the Number of Factory Sellers was Not Smooth, so the Decline was Not Much. As a Result, This Month was Slightly Better Than the Previous Week by 2 Li and a Half. September and October were Smaller by 2 Li and a Half. November was Better by 2 Li and a Half. December was Better by 5 Li. January was Smaller by 2 Li and a Half.

Futures Wheat Declined Consistently.

Yesterday's Futures Wheat Market, Both the Afternoon and Afternoon Market Opening saw Each Month'

Wuhan Disaster Area Epidemic Prevention Work Tense 2

Last night in Hankou, as the water receded slightly, the drowning of rescue workers resulted in punishment.

Liu Ruiheng travels to Hankou by plane.

(Hankou) The city of Hankou has been flooded for half a month, and the water volume increases daily. However, there have been no continued rises since the 17th. Reports of collapsed houses, the spread of epidemics, and electrocutions continue daily. Many people are going downstream to seek refuge. Vessels arrive and depart immediately, still overcrowded. Many wooden embankments in the city have been removed. The bustling markets are having wooden bridges erected by the chamber of commerce to facilitate pedestrian traffic. Epidemic prevention work is particularly tense. Both the medical and educational communities in Wuchang have jointly formed an epidemic prevention association, with Huang Jianzhong and Wang Shijie serving as executive directors. (17th Dispatch)

(Hankou) The Flood Prevention Office stated that rescue workers dispatched by the construction department were perfunctory and negligent. Water conservancy personnel also abandoned their duties. The bureau chief of the said department failed to supervise effectively. Fang Dazhi and Chen Kefang were each given a major demerit as a minor punishment, and they were ordered to submit a list of rescue workers who were ineffective for punishment. Furthermore, the mayor of the city, He Baohua, was given a demerit for neglecting his duty, as employees responsible for reinforcing the levee on the Huangjingtang Sichuan-Hankou railway left their posts without authorization, causing the river water to inundate the levee. He was ordered to personally supervise the staff to go and protect it. The water receded slightly on the evening of the 17th. The water level in the Japanese concession rose, and the electricity was cut off. The lights were also out in a special district, and foreigners boarded ships every night to avoid danger. The lights in the Chinese area remained bright. (17th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) An urgent telegram from Wuchang stated that the river water had entered the Wenchang and Hanyang city gates and caused flooding. (17th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Department of Health dispatched Wang Zuxiang to lead a large number of staff to Hankou to handle epidemic prevention work. (17th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Liu Ruiheng, the Director of the Department of Health, is scheduled to fly to Wuhan on the morning of the 18th for epidemic prevention. (17th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Hubei Province is suffering from floods, and the number of refugees in Wuhan is increasing daily. The Naval Headquarters received a telegram from the Hankou Forward Command stating that the disaster situation is extremely severe, and local order is of utmost importance. The Weisheng warship has been specially dispatched to the vicinity of Jinkou to undertake patrol duties. (17th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Grand Canal Danger Period Has Passed 3

(Nanjing) According to a telegram from an engineer of the Huai River Conservancy Commission stationed at Qinggongpu, the water level in the Grand Canal has receded by two to three feet, and the danger period has passed. (17th Dispatch)

River Water in Shaanxi Continues to Rise 4

(Jinan) The River Affairs Bureau received a telegram from the Yellow River water level station in Shaanxi stating that the water level on the 14th reached 2.58 zhang, which is 54% higher than the highest water level this year. According to this year's highest water level in this province, it is 9.2 zhang above sea level. It is estimated that the water level will rise to 9.2 zhang after the arrival of this water. If it reaches 9.3 zhang, it will be the danger line. The River Affairs Bureau has notified all flood prevention chiefs to inform the local leaders and village chiefs to pay close attention to prevention. (17th Dispatch)

(Jinan) The River Affairs Bureau received a telegram from Shaanxi stating that the water rose another three feet at dawn on the 17th. Today, the water level here is 9.12 zhang above sea level and will inevitably rise to over 9.75 zhang, exceeding the danger line by two feet and breaking previous records. Telegrams from the upper, middle, and lower reaches are urgently reporting the situation. River Affairs Bureau personnel are working through the night to plan emergency measures, fearing a breach. (17th Dispatch)

Zhu Qinglan to Arrive in Beijing Soon

Disaster Relief Committee Considers Food Relief 6

(Nanjing) The Disaster Relief Committee estimates that the national food crisis caused by the current nationwide floods will require the purchase of at least 70 million dan of grain from abroad. At 12 yuan per dan, this will require 850 million yuan. The previous proposal from the United States for a flour loan, as well as the recent telegram from Lin Bai Ke from Beijing, have suggested the same. It is reported that the authorities are considering this. (17th Dispatch)

Ministry of Finance Prepares to Issue Two Types of Treasury Bonds 7

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance has already issued 80 million yuan in Salt Tax Treasury Bonds. However, as disasters are worsening and military expenditures are enormous, it is planning to issue a second batch, with the amount yet to be determined. It is said that it will be named "Continued Issuance of Salt Tax Treasury Bonds." A draft plan for a twenty-year continued issuance of Customs Duty Treasury Bonds is also being pieced together, with the hope of realizing it by the Mid-Autumn Festival. (17th Dispatch)

Shang Zhen Arrives in Beiping Yesterday Morning 8

Telegrams Urge Xu Yongchang to Take Over

(Beiping) Shang Zhen arrived in Beiping this morning. After visiting Zhang Xueliang to report, he plans to seek medical treatment for dysentery in Beiping, so he has received few guests. (17th Dispatch)

(Beiping) Xu Yongchang replied to Shang Zhen via telegram that he had repeatedly been urged to take office, so he had to temporarily maintain the position for a few days. (17th Dispatch)

(Taiyuan) Ge Jingen arrived in Taiyuan on the evening of the 16th, and Xu and others went to welcome him. On the afternoon of the 17th, Ge visited Xu and various generals. He had already reached an agreement with Xu on the political situation and troop deployments in Shanxi. According to Ge, Chiang is extremely concerned about matters in Shanxi. Currently, financial public bonds have been issued, and most of the passenger trains have been dispatched. Both major difficulties have been resolved. The situation in Shanxi should be optimistic from now on. After I consult with Chairman Xu, I will return to Beijing in about three to five days to report, and all follow-up matters can have concrete decisions. (17th Dispatch)

(Beiping) Shang Zhen will not return to Shijiazhuang for the time being. The affairs of the General Headquarters will be handled by Chief of Staff Lü Ji as his proxy. (17th Dispatch)

(Beiping) Li Jingrong, Secretary-General of the Shanxi Provincial Government, arrived in Beiping this morning at the same time as Shang Zhen. Li said that Xu Yongchang had not yet officially taken over the position. I have completed the procedures that should be handed over and can hand them over at any time. Xu stated that he has a comprehensive plan for the Shanxi political situation. After consulting with Ge Jingen and Bao Wenwei as soon as possible, he will travel from Mount Wutai to Datong and then to Beiping to visit Zhang Xueliang. After returning to Taiyuan, he will set a date for taking over. The Shanxi Provincial Government will still be handled by Qiu Yantian, the acting chairman. The handover of the Provincial Government can be handled by Qiu, and the section chiefs of the Secretariat Office can be responsible. I plan to rest in Beiping and will not return to Taiyuan for the time being. (17th Dispatch)

The Northeast Side Is Willing to Fully Guarantee It

(Beiping) Zhang Yinwu returned to his hometown of Boye after the defeat of the Shanxi army to lecture. Recently, his health has been slightly unwell. Chu Xichun will travel from Shanxi to Shijiazhuang and then to Boye to meet Zhang. (17th Dispatch)

(Beiping) After Yan Xishan's defeat, all of the personnel of his Shanxi headquarters were dismissed and returned to their hometowns. In recent years, they have been extremely embarrassed. Ji'an and Other County Towns Rebuilt

(Nanjing) Wei Lihuang's troops recaptured Huangpi, killing more than 1,000 bandits, capturing more than 1,000 alive, and seizing more than 1,000 guns. The remaining bandits fled northwest. (17th Dispatch)

(Nanchang) Three to four thousand pseudo-Red Guard and Guard Battalion vanguards from Toubeiwei, armed with more than a thousand assorted guns, were annihilated by the Right Wing Army. The bodies were piled up, and the remaining bandits hid in the deep mountains. (16th Dispatch)

(Nanchang) Jiang Dingwen telegraphed that more than 1,000 hidden bandits in Changleguan, Bijia Mountain, and Yangshan in Xingguo were attacked on the 11th from Nanxiang Temple and that 500 bandits were killed on the 12th, and the bandits scattered. (16th Dispatch)

(Nanchang) On the 15th, Luo Zhuoying pursued bandits from Junbu to Kongruan. The bandits, together with Xiang bandits and local peasant bandits, relied on the terrain to resist fiercely. Luo's troops launched a fierce attack, and the bandits suffered heavy casualties. Then, the reserve team charged and killed more than 1,000 bandits. (16th Dispatch)

(Nanchang) Aircraft reports (A) Continuous bombing of Gaoxingwei, Shuikou, Longping, Yongfengwei, and the major mountains in the northwest has resulted in countless bandit casualties. (B) Our garrison troops are stationed in Ganghe, Longgang, Toubei, Huangpi, Xiaobu, and Nankeng. There is no trace of bandits east of Huangpi. Captured bandits confessed that the Red bandits collected remnants and made a desperate gamble in Huangpi Xiaopu and the previous battles of Longgang and Liangcun, with casualties reaching two-thirds. (16th Dispatch)

(Nanchang) The city walls that were previously demolished in Ji'an and other counties have all been repaired. The Party and government councils have issued a general order to seriously reorganize the security corps and police force and have formulated seven reorganization measures. (16th Dispatch)

(Nanchang) Lotus and Yongxin have been occupied by Red bandits for several years, and the burning and killings have been extremely tragic. A meeting was held to resolve to petition the headquarters to quickly recapture them to save the survivors. (16th Dispatch)

(Nanchang) The bandits fleeing west are not the main force of Zhu and Mao and are not a problem. Li Mingrui and Liu Tiechao's bandits are still hiding on the west bank of the Gan River, and Kong's bandits are appearing in the border area of Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi. (16th Dispatch)

The Twentieth Annual National Income Budget 24

Is Nearly 100 Million Short

(Nanjing) The twentieth annual national income general budget has been sent to the Comptroller's Office of the National Government. Due to the abolition of likin, revenue is short by 10 million. In addition, customs duties and parcel taxes are short by 19 million yuan annually. The total number of years short is nearly 100 million yuan. There are currently no accurate statistics on the total annual revenue of the newly established consolidated tax. Since March of this year, the salt tax and surtax of various provinces have been collected by the central government. The administrative expenses of each province are then subsidized separately by the central government. Recently, the telegrams from various provinces requesting funds have been accumulated like mountains, and it is impossible to cope with them without issuing new treasury bonds. (17th Dispatch)

Gold Standard Steps 25

(Nanjing) The first step in the gold standard is to determine the national currency, and the second step is to unify the national monetary system. All kinds of currency are unified by the central mint, and provinces are not allowed to mint them separately. If a fictitious gold standard is implemented as a transition, the preparation of cash reserves must be planned first, and implementation is still far away. (17th Dispatch)

It has been submitted to the State Council to ask the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to urge the Japanese government to implement the inspection as soon as possible. (17th Dispatch)

Local News

Unprecedented Flood Disaster, Current Status of River Transportation 55

Hankou in Critical Condition, Trial Navigation on Inland Rivers

This flood disaster has affected as many as sixteen provinces, with the Yangtze River and the Grand Canal being the worst affected. Hankou has been completely submerged, with the city destroyed and transportation completely blocked. However, some of the inland river steamers in Shanghai have been able to resume navigation. The following is a report on the situation obtained by reporters yesterday.

Hankou Submerged, Transportation Blocked 56

Warehouses Completely Submerged. Yesterday, various shipping companies in Shanghai received urgent telegrams from Hankou stating that the river water had risen sharply in recent days, exceeding 55 feet 6 inches. The entire city of Hankou is completely submerged, and the first floors of the docks and warehouses of various shipping companies are underwater. Office personnel from various companies have moved to the top floors, and transportation is entirely by boat. The shallow warehouses are submerged by as much as 15 feet, with countless goods floating away and losses beyond measure. Foreign shipping companies such as Jardine Matheson and Butterfield & Swire have built sky bridges on the docks, directly connecting the ship sides to the second and third floors of the warehouses to facilitate the loading and unloading of goods, bypassing the floodwaters in the city.

Construction of Wooden Towers. The China Merchants Bureau received a telegram from Hankou stating that the water depth along the docks reaches over 10 feet. The branch manager, Li Yunliang, has purchased giant timbers worth over 10,000 yuan and is building a wooden tower in front of the dockside warehouse. The purpose of the tower is to prevent further flooding. The tower will have large overhanging beams, so that when a ship arrives, one end will reach the upper level of the warehouse and the other end will reach the ship's deck, allowing goods to be loaded and unloaded over the water into the warehouse. It is currently being built day and night, and will soon be ready for practical use, facilitating the loading and unloading of goods and passengers.

Dormitories Submerged. Yesterday, it was confirmed that the two dormitory buildings occupied by Jardine Matheson's employees in Hankou have disappeared without a trace, completely submerged in the floodwaters. Only the tops of the large trees in Hankou Park are still visible above the water, and the buildings have long since vanished.

Preparing Ships for Emergency. The lower-level offices of foreign shipping companies such as Butterfield & Swire, Jardine Matheson, Nissin Kisen, Chekiang River Steamship Co., and China Merchants S.N. Co. in Hankou have all been submerged and moved to the second and third floors to operate. However, as the river water continues to rise, the companies fear further flooding and have each dispatched an empty river steamer to the docks since the 15th, ready for employees to board and evacuate in case of emergency. The China Merchants Bureau also sent an urgent telegram to Shanghai ordering a large river steamer to be dispatched to provide refuge for bureau employees in case of emergency.

Complete Interruption of Goods. Goods arriving via the Pinghan Railway have been cut off for some time. River goods from Yichang and Sichuan are also unable to be shipped due to the floods. Only a small number of goods from Hunan are being transshipped. Goods are almost completely cut off. However, thousands of flood-stricken refugees from Hankou, affected by the rising waters, have been fleeing downstream. In recent days, Chinese merchant river steamers departing from Hankou have been filled with refugees. Crew members cannot drive them away, even though they cannot afford tickets. Most of them are disembarking in Jiangxi and Anhui, and relatively few are coming to Shanghai. The compradores on each ship are suffering huge losses, but there is nothing they can do.

First Phase Opening of Inland Water Ferries 57

Due to the flooding, the Shanghai-Suzhou line operated by the local inland water ferry companies had been suspended since July 6th, resulting in significant losses for each company for over forty days. China Merchants Steam Navigation Company (招商局) suffered daily losses of approximately six to seven hundred yuan, while Da Sheng Chang (戴生昌) lost three hundred yuan daily, and other companies lost between one and two hundred yuan. Recent surveys by the companies have determined that the Shanghai-Suzhou route can be partially reopened. Yesterday, China Merchants Steam Navigation Company assigned the Li Heng (利亨) ferry, and Da Sheng Chang assigned the Yuan Yu (原餘) and Da An (大安) ferries, etc., to resume operations on the first two days. Passengers are advised that only slow ferries will be available along the route.

The Shanghai-Hangzhou trial route was also suspended because of the numerous bridges and high water levels that made passage difficult. Recent reports indicate that the water level has slightly receded. China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Da Sheng Chang, and Lao Gong Mao (老公茂) have agreed to dispatch the Heng Shun (恒順), Heng Sheng (恒勝), Yuan Fa (源發), and Yuan Ji (源吉) ferries starting today for a trial run from Shanghai. A formal resumption of operations will be scheduled after it is determined that there are no obstructions along the route.

The Shanghai-Lake Tai (申湖) route, operated by six ferry companies offering both day and night services, has also been suspended for a long time. It has recently been reported that the Tian, Di, Yuan, and Huang sections of Lake Tai in Huzhou have been completely submerged. In the Li Li area, the water level has slightly receded. The six companies have decided to fully resume both day and night ferry services within the next two days. Personnel have already been dispatched via civilian boats to survey various locations in preparation for the resumption of operations.

The Shanghai-Ling (申菱) route to Jiaxing can reportedly barely accommodate boat travel. China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has dispatched the Xin An (新安) ferry to resume operations. The water level on the Jiaxing-Lake Tai (嘉湖) route has also slightly decreased. Yesterday, the Cheng Tai (承泰) ferry was also ordered to resume operations. As for the Shanghai-Wuxi (申錫) route, ferries will continue to operate in conjunction, with one route to Kunshan and the other to Dunhe. Passengers will be transferred between boats in the middle.

The Shanghai-Changzhou (申常) route remains closed due to the high water level. According to the companies, it will take at least two weeks before operations can resume. The water level on the Zhenjiang-Yangzhou (鎭揚) route is only subtly rising. This route is not expected to resume operations until September at the earliest. Of the thirty-plus inland water ferry routes, only the Shanghai-Suzhou, Shanghai-Hangzhou, Shanghai-Lake Tai, Shanghai-Jiaxing, and Shanghai-Ling routes have been partially reopened.

Yesterday's Emergency Relief Meeting for Flood Disaster Discussed Fundraising Strategies 58

According to Huadong News Agency, the Shanghai Emergency Relief Association for Flood Disasters in Various Provinces held a discussion meeting at the City Chamber of Commerce yesterday afternoon to determine fundraising strategies. The meeting discussed implementation methods until about 7 PM. The details are summarized as follows:

Attendees: The meeting was attended by a large number of people, including Xu Shiying, Chairman of the Relief Committee; Wang Zhen, Vice Chairman; Zhang Zhijiang, Pacification Commissioner of the Jiangsu Pacification Commissioner's Office; Jiang Zuobin, the newly appointed Ambassador to Japan; as well as Wang Xiaolai, Wu Zhihao, Zhang Zhuping, Lin Kanghou, Wen Lanting, Zhuang Songfu, Li Zushen, Hong Yingbin, Huang Renzhi, Zhu Hui Seng, Li Cishan, Wang Boyuan, and dozens of others.

Discussion Agenda: (1) Electing a temporary chairman; (2) Reporting on disaster reports and requests for funds from various provinces; (3) Reporting on the recent work of the association; (4) Requesting representatives from various sectors to provide lists for distribution of donation booklets for fundraising; (5) Discussing fundraising methods; (6) Setting deadlines for pledged donations to be submitted to the association; (7) The association should first select the most severely affected areas for emergency relief; (8) Adjournment.

Discussion Summary: After formal greetings, Xu Shiying, Chairman of the Relief Committee, was elected as the temporary chairman. The chairman reported on the disaster situation in various provinces and recent requests for funds. Wang Xiaolai then reported on the recent work of the association. Subsequently, fundraising methods were discussed and donation booklets were distributed. Zhuang Songfu, Wu Zhihao, Hong Yanbin, Zhang Zhuping, Yu Daxiong, and others proposed fundraising suggestions.

Important Proposals: Many attendees expressed their opinions. The following proposals were submitted to the conference and passed: (A) Huang Yanpei proposed: (1) The massive flooding in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River will inevitably turn the downstream provinces and counties into a vast swamp within a few days. Jiangsu and Anhui have already reported disasters, and more serious emergencies are expected. How can we prevent them as much as possible? (2) To conduct large-scale fundraising and achieve significant results, we must start with the business income, property income, and personal salaries of various sectors and industries to arouse enthusiastic emotions from all parties. We must especially encourage our executive committee members to take the lead. If our committee members agree with this proposal, each member should report a certain percentage of their business or property income, or one or two months, or at least half a month of their personal salary. The resolution should be published in newspapers to arouse sympathy from all parties. Then, we should approach the owners of properties, such as houses, for fundraising without coercion. Since everyone desires to do good, we will surely achieve greater results. (B) Zhang Zhuping proposed: (1) Commercial organizations should contribute a certain percentage of their annual business income as donations. It is best if commercial organizations do this voluntarily, while the association formulates methods for implementation. (2) A certain percentage of the salaries of employees of commercial institutions should be contributed as disaster relief donations. The method should be the same as above. (C) Hong Yanbin proposed: (1) Hold a fundraising commemorative week; (2) First, borrow cash from the banking and financial industries to meet the needs of emergency relief. (D) Chu Hui Seng proposed: Focus on fundraising by industry, with donations set at one-fourth of one month's income. (2) Raise donations from schools: elementary school students donate 20 cents each, junior high school students donate 50 cents each, and high school students and above donate one yuan each. Faculty and staff should donate according to their abilities. (E) Wu Zhihao proposed: (1) Advocate for businesses to donate 5% or 10% of their seven-day revenue. A separate fundraising method should be established for non-retail businesses. (2) Free professional organizations should organize fundraising committees. (3) The press should organize a publicity committee. (F) Yu Daxiong proposed: Solicit disaster relief plans through newspaper advertisements. All of the above proposals were unanimously approved by the conference. Except for the organization of the publicity committee, which was decided to be the responsibility of Zhang Zhuping, and the immediate solicitation of fundraising plans through newspaper advertisements, the remaining proposals were immediately handed over to the association's standing committee for immediate action.

Adding Committee Members: Yesterday's meeting also added committee members to strengthen the association's internal organization: (1) Li Cishan, Huang Renzhi, Huang Yanfang, Wu Yunzhai, Wu Zhihao, Qin Runqing, Wang Boyuan, Zhang Zhuping, Hong Yanbin, Chu Hui Seng, Li Zuyu, Zhuang Songfu, Sun Choucheng, and Wang Yunzhang were appointed as members of the conference's design group. (2) Wang Xiaolai, Hong Yanbin, Cao Zhigong, Zheng Chengqing, Jin Guanfu, Zhang Yichen, Hu Fengxiang, Wang Pingnan, Chen Liting, and Lin Kanghou were appointed to be in charge of fundraising methods. (3) Zhang Zhuping and Dong Xian Guang were appointed as publicity committee members. (4) Xu Yongzuo and Pan Xulun were appointed as economic audit committee members for the conference.

City Scouts Launch Fundraising for Disaster Relief 59

Organize Fundraising Committee, Meeting Held Yesterday to Determine Methods

The 383rd Regiment of the China Boy Scouts, deeply concerned about the recent floods that have turned the area into a swamp, with countless people drowned and adrift, could not bear to stand idly by. The group petitioned the Shanghai City Council of the China Boy Scouts to launch a fundraising campaign as soon as possible to provide emergency relief. After receiving the petition, the City Council approved the request at its 20th standing meeting and appointed Tong Xingbai, Xu Peihuang, Shen Yu, Wang Gang, Leng Xueqiao, Qu Yue, Huang Shan, Luo Lie, and Wu Chuliang as members of the Shanghai Boy Scouts Disaster Relief Fundraising Committee to handle the matter. Wang Gang was designated as the convener. The 10th standing meeting was held at the Shanghai China Junior High School at 2 PM yesterday to discuss implementation methods. The results are summarized as follows: (1) Determining the Name of the Association: It was decided to name it the "Shanghai Boy Scouts Flood Disaster Relief Fundraising Committee." (2) How to Determine Fundraising Methods: It was decided that all city boy scouts would conduct street fundraising and hold a city-wide boy scout entertainment show. (3) Determining the Organization of the Association: It was decided to divide it into a Standing Committee, Entertainment Section, Fundraising Section, Publicity Section, Social Section, Accounting Section, and Affairs Section. The Standing Committee would be composed of three members of the committee. Each section would have one committee member in charge. (4) Selecting Standing Committee Members: It was decided to select Tong Xingbai, Xu Peihuang, and Wang Gang. (5) Selecting Section Heads: It was decided to select Qu Yue as the head of the Entertainment Section, Shen Yu as the head of the Publicity Section, Huang Shan as the head of the Social Section, Wu Chuliang as the head of the Accounting Section, Leng Xueqiao as the head of the Fundraising Section, and Luo Lie as the head of the Affairs Section. (6) Designating a Bank for Deposits: It was decided to use the Shanghai Bank. (7) Determining the Date of Regular Meetings: It was decided to hold meetings every Monday at 8 AM. (8) Drafting the Association's Organizational and Work Plan Outline: It was decided to appoint Shen Yu to draft the association's organizational outline and Wang Gang to draft the association's work plan. (9) How to Raise Funds for the Association's Expenses: It was decided to request the City Council to temporarily advance funds, which would be deducted from the fundraising proceeds in the future. The meeting adjourned after the discussions.

Memorial Service for Mother Song 60

Hundreds from All Walks of Life Attended, Zhang Qun Represented the National Government to Offer Condolences

Yesterday was the day of the memorial service for Mother Song, Madam Ni. The mourning hall was set up in the living room outside the Song residence on Seymour Road. A horizontal plaque with the words "Loyalty and Service to the Nation" (敎忠報國) granted by the National Government hung outside the hall. The mourning hall was filled with wreaths and elegiac couplets, creating a solemn atmosphere. From 8 AM to 6 PM yesterday, Chinese and foreign guests came to pay their respects in an endless stream, including Zhao Jinqing, Zhang Qun, Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yiting, Du Yuesheng, Japanese Ambassador Shigemitsu Mamoru, and consuls from various countries, totaling several hundred people. The public memorial service began at 12:30 PM. The order of the public memorial service was as follows: (1) The officiant takes his place; (2) The participants take their places; (3) Stand in silence; (4) Play mournful music; (5) The officiant offers flowers; (6) Read the eulogy; (7) Perform three bows; (8) The filial sons offer thanks; (9) The ceremony concludes; (10) Play music. (15) Zhang Shuxian representing Xiong Xiling; (16) Representatives of the Shanghai Banking Association, Chamber of Commerce, and Taxpaying Chinese Association; (17) Representatives of the Exchange Federation, Yarn Factory, Flour Mill Association, and other organizations. You were born in the spiritual lands of Puzhu and embodied the beauty of Mount Luofu. In your youth, you showed gentleness and virtue, and in your adulthood, you were known for your prudence and diligence. You knew the labor of gathering reeds and the reverence of picking water chestnuts. You assisted your husband in managing affairs in all directions, and together you soared ten thousand miles, like linked jade and a harmonious union. You taught with righteousness and thoroughness. You sealed your honor and cherished integrity, and nurtured aspirations like Mengmu moving three times. Your dignified demeanor and reputation spread far and wide. You were cared for with respect and joy in your old age, and you enjoyed the scenic beauty of the mountains with a cane. The nine peaks were shrouded in mist, and the two peaks of Mount Lao were green. Suddenly, you left this world and returned to your true home. People cherish your virtuous model, and the nation praises your merits. A mound on Longgang records your virtue, and history will praise your legacy. Your generation's mourning is splendid and follows the rules. We pour wine and offer words, may your spirit accept them. May you enjoy this sacrifice."

The City Chamber of Commerce Hosts a Banquet for the American Chamber of Commerce Travel Group 63

Both Hosts and Guests Gave Sincere Speeches

The City Chamber of Commerce hosted a banquet for the American Chamber of Commerce of Los Angeles Travel Group at the Chamber's regular meeting room at noon yesterday. More than fifty Chinese and foreign guests attended, including Guo Bingan, Guo Binwen, Wang Xiaolai, Lin Kanghou, and Xu Xinliu. Wang Xiaolai, Chairman of the Chamber, delivered a speech, followed by a response from the representative of the travel group. After the meeting, the Chamber's committee members accompanied the travel group to visit the Chamber's product exhibition hall and the domestic goods market, where they purchased many domestic products. The speeches are recorded as follows:

The City Chamber of Commerce's welcome speech briefly stated that although the history of trade between China and the United States spans eight or ninety years, both countries are vast and rich in resources, and their populations are large. In the past, transportation was not very convenient, so there were few opportunities for contact between the people of the two countries, except for those who traded in each other's countries. Americans who wanted to understand the situation in China could only learn from books and magazines. However, the authors of these books and magazines may not have had an accurate understanding of the situation in China, or the information may have been outdated or limited to a local perspective, which was insufficient to represent the whole country. Therefore, there were very few Americans who had a genuine understanding of the situation in China. It is regrettable that after more than eighty years of diplomatic relations, the situation remains unclear. Therefore, the Chamber believes that to bridge the gap between each other, there should be continuous mutual visits and travel, especially for a longer period of time. The longer the visit, the easier it will be to thoroughly understand each other's situation, which is different from a hurried visit. It is said that the travel group will purchase Chinese products as a souvenir of this trip. The Chamber believes that this is of great significance because the foundation of the friendly relations between China and the United States for more than eighty years is built on "only seeking trade without other purposes." Therefore, the travel group's purchase of our country's products as a souvenir of their trip best demonstrates the true meaning of the lasting friendship between the two countries. On the other hand, it can show the actual situation of China's recent industrial progress. When the travel group returns and presents the souvenirs to relatives and friends, it can also allow the American people to spread and understand that China has indeed been engaged in peaceful construction in industry and commerce in recent years, so that the people of the two countries can build a new foundation for their diplomatic psychology. This trip can also lead the American people to have a deep impression of the goods that they need and that China can supply, and jointly work on the reform of tariff policies so that both Chinese manufacturers and American consumers can be satisfied. This is all thanks to the travel group's visit.

The City Chamber of Commerce Hosts a Banquet for the American Chamber of Commerce Travel Group (Photo by This Newspaper) 64

The American travel group's response briefly stated that it is a great pleasure that the people of China and the United States can gather together today. At the same time, they thank the Chamber for the lavish banquet and kind hospitality. The speaker represents the Los Angeles Chamber of Commerce travel group and various business circles in Southern California to come to the Far East to investigate business and sightseeing. The purpose is to expand the commercial shipping between Southern California and the East. This sightseeing is not the end, and there will likely be other sightseeing groups coming one after another in the future. They hope that your country will also come to our country for inspection from time to time. Former US President Roosevelt once said that there are three major periods in the world: one is the Mediterranean period, which has become a past period; the second is the Atlantic period, which is nearing its end; and the third is the Pacific period, which is in full swing. Mr. O'Malley's speech in the United States in 1915 also said that the prosperous period of the Pacific has arrived. Therefore, I believe that China has made great contributions to the development of the Pacific. In the first week of May next year, the National Commercial Association of the United States will hold a conference in Honolulu to discuss all commercial issues along the Pacific coast. The solution to this problem is the realization of the new Pacific landscape in a few years and thousands of years. We deeply hope that your country can join and submit what you want to discuss and what you hope for at that time. We also hope that China can send more athletes to participate in the World Games in 1932.

The eastern, western, and northern sides of the county have been flooded by the Yangtze River. Ninety-six dikes and thirteen islands have collapsed, and more than 30,000 villages and more than 170,000 disaster victims have been submerged. It is almost like selling children and selling daughters to survive in the waves. It is an unprecedentedly tragic situation. We dare to ask kind people and philanthropists to gather strength and provide clothing and bedding for the people. Every drop of water is a life-saving pill, and tears and blood make up the picture of the refugees. Tongling County Flood Relief Committee in Shanghai kowtows."

The chairman approved all of the above before adjourning the meeting.

Sichuan: The Sichuan Fellow Townsmen Association in Shanghai sent a telegram to the Nanjing Relief Committee, saying: "The telegraph has been delivered. The flood disaster in Sichuan this time, according to reports from hometown letters, the areas in eastern and southern Sichuan that have been passed through by the tributaries of the Yangtze River have mostly suffered from the collapse of fields and crops, and the destruction of homes. It is a tragic situation that has not been seen in a hundred years. Among them, the situation is particularly severe in Hejiang in southern Sichuan, where eleven of the sixteen districts in the entire county have been submerged in water. Other areas in the Jiang area have also suffered from strong winds and hailstorms. Tonggu and Gulin counties have also been completely submerged, and almost no peaks can be seen. In Xiushan and Pengshui in eastern Sichuan, the water is nine feet high, and the plains have become rivers. In addition to the complete destruction of the salt fields and stoves, more than 1,000 elderly and children have been drowned, more than 3,000 houses have collapsed, and more than 2,000 acres of fields have been destroyed. It is particularly tragic to see. However, due to traffic congestion, the details have not yet been heard outside Sichuan. The association is appealing for relief from all parties. We have also received a telegram from Chongqing, saying that the Yangtze River has been rising for days, reaching nearly ten feet. Residents along the river have suffered severe disasters. The association is instructed to find ways to provide relief. The details of the disaster are not yet known at this time. However, considering that the downstream Wuhan is so severely affected, the flooded areas upstream can be imagined. Our Sichuan people are suffering from both a rice shortage and this disaster. The only thing they can look forward to is the relief from the central government. However, we read in the newspaper yesterday that the conference only allocated 10,000 yuan to Sichuan for emergency relief. The conference has its own difficulties. However, with more than one million disaster victims sharing this 10,000 yuan for emergency relief, it is indeed unable to meet the urgent needs. The conference is the center for national relief, and it is said that it treats everyone equally. We hope that you will look west and not forget the distant ones. Allocating one more yuan for relief can save one more life. Saving one more life can add one more merit. Therefore, we cannot help but earnestly ask you to pay special attention and give generously to rescue our people from the sea of suffering. If you can think deeply about the people's suffering and convey the will of the people to the central government in a timely manner to urge it to withdraw the order to issue Sichuan bonds and stop the Sichuan warlords from levying exorbitant taxes, then it will be the fundamental relief for our people, and its merit will be above emergency relief. The telegraph is urgent. I hope you will consider it carefully. Sichuan Fellow Townsmen Association in Shanghai kowtows."

Application Period for Sun Yat-sen Stamps 70

Submitted by the Directorate General of Posts for Ministry Approval

Regarding the issue of the new Sun Yat-sen stamps, which were shipped to Shanghai from the British printing company De La Rue on September 1 for use in postal areas nationwide, a reporter from the Guowen News Agency interviewed Mr. Han Zhongyi of the Secretariat of the Directorate General of Posts yesterday to inquire about the procedures. The reply was as follows:

The request has been submitted to the Ministry for approval. This time, the British printing company shipped 120 million Sun Yat-sen stamps to Shanghai. Subsequently, they will be shipped in monthly installments to reach a total of 300 million stamps annually. Because this is the first batch, the quantity is relatively large. The Directorate General has submitted a request to the Ministry to designate September 1 as the date for the implementation of the new one-cent, two-cent, four-cent, and two-jiao four-cent Sun Yat-sen stamps. It is expected that the Ministry will issue instructions soon. Currently, the Directorate General will continue to use all kinds of ordinary stamps with sailing ships and farmers as before until they are exhausted.

The preparation for distributing the required stamps to postal areas nationwide is usually handled by the Shanghai Postal Supply Office on Jiaozhou Road in this city. However, the scope of the postal areas nationwide is vast, and the needs of each area are inconsistent. The preparations for the distribution of the new Sun Yat-sen stamps this time will require detailed investigation and planning for different combinations. No statistical reports have yet been received by the bureau.

Regarding the situation of square-printed stamps, the Beiping Printing and Mint Bureau of the Ministry of Finance has been entrusted with printing six kinds of stamps of revolutionary martyrs Huang Kecheng, Song Jiaoren, Deng Keng, Liao Zhongkai, Zhu Zhixin, and Chen Yingshi. It is heard that they are already in production. Shen Nengyi, the director of the Beiping Printing Bureau, has come to Shanghai but has not yet contacted the bureau. Therefore, the quantity of these new martyr stamps that need to be printed each year and the cost of printing each year are not yet very clear.

Denominations of new stamps: The fixed denominations of the Sun Yat-sen stamps are one cent, two cents, four cents, two jiao, one yuan, two yuan, five yuan, and seven yuan. The one-yuan to five-yuan denominations are specially prepared for postage of parcels, overweight envelopes, and insured letters, and are not the yuan stamps counted in money orders. The six kinds of martyr stamps are divided into twelve denominations: half-cent, two-and-a-half cents, five cents, six cents, eight cents, one jiao, one jiao five cents, one jiao six cents, two jiao five cents, three jiao, four jiao, and five jiao. Each kind of martyr stamp is printed in two kinds. Because the bureau has not yet received any formal documents from the Beiping Printing Bureau on how the square-printed stamps are allocated and printed, there is no way to verify them.

Twenty-three postal districts nationwide: The national postal district plan has twenty-three locations. Some provinces are one district, some are two provinces combined into one district, or one province is divided into two districts that also administer other districts. According to the reporter's investigation, the following is a list: Jiangsu-Anhui District (Capital), Shanghai District, Zhejiang District (Hangzhou), Fujian District (Min County), Guangdong District (Guangzhou), Guangxi District (Nanning), Gansu District (Lanzhou), Shaanxi District (Xi'an), Guizhou District (Guiyang), Henan District (Kaifeng), Hubei District (Hankou), Hunan District (Changsha), Eastern Sichuan District (Chongqing), Western Sichuan District (Chengdu, including Xikang Province), Xinjiang District (Dihua, including Qinghai jurisdiction), Jiangxi District (Nanchang), Shandong District (Jinan), Hebei District (Tianjin), Beiping District (including Rehe, Chahar, Suiyuan, and Inner Mongolia postal jurisdiction), Liaoning District, Jilin-Heilongjiang District (Binjiang County, i.e., Harbin), Shanxi District (Taiyuan), and Yunnan District (Kunming). It is said that no districts have been established in Tibet and Outer Mongolia.

Dr. Jiang Kanghu's Talk After Returning from the New World 71

Research on Chinese Culture There is More Prosperous Than in the Past

Responsible for Communicating Culture Between the Two Countries This Time

Americans Hope We Can Clear Internal Chaos and Establish Constitution Early

Wrote Gospel of World Recession on the Return Journey

Dr. Jiang Kanghu was hired by the U.S. government in 1927 to serve as a consultant at the Library of Congress to handle Eastern cultural affairs. He was later appointed as the Dean of the Chinese Academy at McGill University in Canada. This time, he returned to China to make contact with the Chinese government authorities. A reporter from the New Voice Society met with Mr. Jiang at his lodging yesterday, and he expressed the following:

Life in the United States: Mr. Jiang has spent four years in the United States specializing in the study of the advantages of Chinese culture and promoting its material aspects to the country as much as possible. He has been greatly praised by people from all walks of life in the United States. After he wrote the History of Chinese Culture, Canada specially established a Chinese Academy and hired Mr. Jiang as the dean to teach Eastern philosophy. Mr. Jiang is the only Chinese person who has recently served as a full professor in universities in Europe and the United States. In addition, he has translated 300 Tang Poems, and when they were translated, they were slightly corrected by famous British and American poets. Therefore, after the book was published, its sales have exceeded 5,000 copies. Purchasers from Britain and Japan are also numerous. The book is currently sold at other bookstores on Nanjing Road in Shanghai. In addition to teaching and writing, Mr. Jiang is invited to give public lectures more than 50 times a year. According to Mr. Jiang, the number of Americans studying Chinese culture is increasing day by day, and their interest is also greater than before.

Mission of Returning to China: One reason for returning to China this time is that he has been abroad for a long time and has many gaps in his understanding of the domestic situation. Although he usually sees it in newspapers, it is often inaccurate and slow, and there is very little correct information. Therefore, he intends to take this opportunity to return to China to see the domestic situation so that he can have a basis for future propaganda in the United States. At the same time, he also intends to meet with relatives, old friends, and family members in Beiping after a long separation to express his accumulated feelings. On the one hand, he is entrusted by the U.S. government to make further consultations on the cultural communication between China and the United States. He will request the Chinese government authorities and educational institutions to allow the transportation of valuable circulations, related to the history of culture, which are not isolated books, to the United States to be used for public research in the U.S. National Library. This will allow the United States to see the bright culture and national spirit of our country's history, and a glorious cultural history of our country for 5,000 years can also be promoted overseas.

Americans' Expectations of Us: Americans have always hoped that our country can be unified nationally and that politics can be put on the right track. However, although people in that country have many doubts about the unstable situation in our country in recent years, they also have no ill will. As for our overseas Chinese in the United States, when they are asked by people in that country about the domestic situation or when they give public speeches, they must explain what Americans are alienated and misunderstood, and the only goal is to let Americans understand the situation in our country, that is, modern China is an inevitable process on the road to revolution, no matter what. However, the goal of the whole country of China is still to seek freedom and equality for China. If you want freedom and equality for China, you must work together to abolish unequal treaties. Therefore, the first hope of Americans for our country is to clear internal chaos and banditry. At the same time, they hope to produce a sound constitution.

World Trends: On this trip, Mr. Jiang wrote an article of about 3,000 words entitled "The Gospel of the World Recession." The main idea is that in the past, the momentum of capitalists was completely due to the selling short and buying long in the exchange, and the result must be failure. The current world recession is the end of the bankruptcy of capitalism. For example, the United States is known as a rich country, but when money is not in circulation, it can only become a mineral. Therefore, since the United States has been in a recession, not only is there no interest in depositing money in banks, but also a handling fee must be paid every year. At the same time, the unemployed who are eliminated due to the recession have no support, so social peace must be greatly affected. The United States is like this, and other countries are also like this. Due to the pressure of the situation, the standard of living in the United States has to be reduced. As far as I know, the United States and Japan have both reduced by a quarter, and as the trend continues, there is no doubt that socialism will be implemented after capitalism collapses. Capitalism is like an airplane in the air, no matter how durable it is, it will eventually have to land. However, the current state of world recession has entered a stage that socialism must go through. Therefore, I said that it is the gospel of the world recession.

Sharp Increase in Cotton Imports 72

According to the news from the Chinese Cotton Mill Federation yesterday, the domestic cotton production in recent years has gradually become insufficient to meet the needs, and as a result, the number of American and Indian cotton imported is very large. The total import of American cotton in Shanghai in 1930 was 1,008,000 dan, and the total import of Indian cotton was 1,508,000 dan, which is the highest record of foreign cotton imported by our country. Unexpectedly, the import this year has increased even more. In the first half of the year ending at the end of June, the import of American cotton reached 619,000 dan, and the import of Indian cotton reached 808,000 dan. Currently, because foreign cotton is cheap, each factory has ordered a huge amount of foreign cotton. It is expected that the import of American and Indian cotton in the second half of the year will be more than the first half of the year, and the total number of American and Indian cotton for the whole year will exceed last year.

The matter has now been completed. He arrived in Shanghai yesterday on the Japanese ship Shanghai Maru.
