Municipal Government Protests Japanese Soldiers' Robbery of Goods, Japanese Consul General's Quibble 74

Denies Japanese Merchants Requested Troops to Protect Goods, Will Respond to Municipal Government by Letter in Two or Three Days

The Shanghai Municipal Government protested to the Japanese Consulate General on the 14th of this month about the unreasonable detention and beating of anti-Japanese aid overseas Chinese committee members by Japanese sailors. The Japanese side has not yet responded to this matter. Yesterday, a reporter from the New Voice Society went to the Consulate General to interview Consul General Murai. According to him, after reading the protest letter from the Municipal Government, he has not yet responded. He will probably respond in two or three days. Before formally responding to the Municipal Government, he cannot inform them of the contents in advance because the reply has not yet been drafted. However, the occurrence of this incident was not caused by the dispatch of troops by the Japanese Consulate or any Japanese agency. When the anti-Japanese association inspectors seized the goods, the merchant requested nearby patrols to protect them. However, the patrols were not present, and if there were Japanese soldiers, these Japanese soldiers would certainly protect the merchants in accordance with the obligations of the military and would never sit idly by. This is the reason. As for the reports in Japanese newspapers that Japanese merchants sent representatives to request the Japanese side to send troops to protect the import or landing of Japanese goods, these are all untrue. It is common for merchants to send representatives to the Consulate General to petition, but they did not request troops to protect the transportation of goods, and the Japanese side has no intention of doing so.

Two Meetings on Resisting Japanese Goods 75

Municipal Chamber of Commerce: The Luxury Goods Group and the Necessary Goods Group of the Resist Japanese Goods Research Committee of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce held their first joint meeting yesterday. More than a dozen committee members, including Ye Jiaxing and Zhang Shengyong, attended. Ye Jiaxing presided over the meeting and resolved the following cases: (1) Discuss the standard for classifying Japanese goods. It was resolved that the classification method can be carried out in two aspects: A. Send a letter to the Anti-Japanese Aid Overseas Chinese Association to borrow the Japanese goods survey booklet and have the association reprint and distribute it to each committee member for research. B. Send a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to forward it to the Jianghai Customs to extract the detailed items of imported Japanese goods and have the association print and distribute them to each group for review as the standard for future classification research. (2) Discuss the letter from the Coal Industry Association inquiring about the Japanese coal registration method. It was resolved that Japanese coal should be handled in accordance with the necessary goods treatment method before the domestic products are fully self-sufficient. The fund levy rate will be determined after research. (3) Discuss the letter from the medicinal materials industry association stating that Japanese medicinal materials are irreplaceable and request research. It was resolved that the items opened in the letter will be handed over to the inspection committee for investigation to verify whether they are true before further review. (4) Discuss how the meeting date of this group should be stipulated. It was resolved that it should be held on Monday afternoon at 1:00 p.m. sharp every week.

Anti-Japanese Association: The Design Committee of the Anti-Japanese Association held its fifth committee meeting in the conference room of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. Fourteen committee members, including Zhu Wenqi, Cai Guo Jingluan, Li Wenjie, Feng Yixian, Ping Zhi, Zhang Peizhen, Lu Fengzhu, Pan Xulun, Xu Yongzuo, Kui Yanfang, Chen Songyuan, and Deng Zena attended. Zhu Wenqi was elected chairman and resolved the following cases: (1) Discuss the paper industry association's plan to resist foreign paper. It was resolved to hand it over to the drafter of the five-year industrial plan for reference. (2) Discuss the proposal by Committee Member Deng Zena to deal with the root causes of resisting Japanese sugar. It was resolved: A. Hand it over to the drafter of the five-year industrial plan for reference. B. Send a letter to the Guangdong Committee to suggest it to the Ministries of Finance. (3) Discuss the request from the Great China Match Company to copy and attach the names and quantities of the Japanese goods they need for verification. It was resolved to handle it in accordance with the industrial raw material regulations. (4) Discuss how to handle the fact that the paper materials used by the China Arts and Crafts Factory are a special product of Japan and there are no substitutes in other countries, let alone domestic goods. It was resolved to first have the factory send a letter to the paper industry association to find out whether there are domestic substitutes before further review. Finally, after a long discussion on the issue of drafting the five-year industrial plan, the meeting adjourned.

Second Propaganda Meeting of the Anti-Japanese Aid Overseas Chinese Association 76

Chen Binhe Lectures on Anti-Japanese and Knowing Japan

According to the New Voice Society, the second propaganda meeting of the Shanghai Anti-Japanese Aid Overseas Chinese Congress was held at 3 p.m. yesterday in the auditorium of the YMCA on Sichuan Road. A large number of people participated enthusiastically. After the ceremony, Chairman Lu Jingshi gave a speech reporting on everything, and then invited Mr. Chen Binhe to give a lecture entitled "Anti-Japanese and Knowing Japan." Chen has expertise in the study of the Japanese Manchurian problem and has published the Japanese Research Monthly. His speech roughly stated: The topic I am going to talk about today is "Anti-Japanese." If British and French people were to talk about it, they might say, "The Chinese nation is a scattered nation with no complete organization and no spirit of collective effort. It should be bullied by others and should be preyed upon by others. The Japanese are not like this. Not only do they have the qualifications to be masters, but they also have the qualifications to be leaders." If Japanese people were to talk about it, they would definitely say, "The Chinese are too humble and often think that unimportant things are terrible." However, this problem is being spoken to Chinese people, and the audience is also Chinese people. Everyone knows that the motive for this anti-Japanese movement is the Wanbaoshan incident, and the origin of the Wanbaoshan incident was caused by the Japanese expelling Koreans from the country to carry out their aggressive conspiracy. The massacre of overseas Chinese in Korea was caused by excessive propaganda, manipulation, and instigation. Everyone, how pitiful and embarrassing is our Chinese position? Even the news of the detention of four anti-Japanese association inspectors on the 12th, is this something we should endure? Is this something that should be in our position? Speaking of economic severance, there have been eight times in history. The first time was in 1908, the 34th year of Guangxu, because of the smuggling of military supplies. The second time was in 1909, the first year of Xuantong, because the Japanese expanded their route in the Northeast. The third time was in 1915, the 4th year of the Republic of China, because of the non-recognition of the Twenty-One Demands. The fourth time was in 1919, the 8th year of the Republic of China, because of the Shandong problem. The fifth time was in 1923, the 12th year of the Republic of China, because of the recovery of Lushun and Dalian. The sixth time was in 1925, the 14th year of the Republic of China, because of the May 30th massacre. The seventh time was in 1928, because of the Jinan massacre. The eighth time is now. Each time can prove what our results are. From the perspective of Sino-Japanese international trade, it can be seen that each time has suffered a major blow, while the Japanese have said, "Your resistance has absolutely nothing to do with us." A part of the Chinese people has also echoed this due to the counter-propaganda of Japanese imperialism. However, I dare to believe that the Sino-Japanese economic relationship is very important and can definitely be implemented based on Mr. Liang Sibing's article in the July 29th Current Affairs News, "The Practical Effect of Resisting Japanese Goods," and Mr. DrcbareI's article in the August issue of the Current Affairs Monthly, "China Uses Resisting Foreign Goods as a Foreign Weapon," because China is Japan's second largest market and Japan's supply place. We don't have military power to resist him. We only have the method of economic severance that is more feasible. I further think that even if the method of economic severance has a loss, we are still better than the failure of military resistance. In Sino-Japanese trade, from 1868 (the third year of Tongzhi) to 1930, there have been 64 years. Except for 1870, 1891, 1892, 1893, and 1894-5, China has been exporting, and the rest have been importing from Japan. The Shanghai Machinery Federation has a saying: "The way for us to save ourselves is to adopt a policy of self-sufficiency and self-reliance, strive to create production, and stop the source. There is no obvious form of resistance, but there is the effect of developing industry. Speaking of saving the country, there is nothing better than this." I very much agree with this statement, and I think this is the only method of self-determination for our anti-Japanese movement, because resisting Japanese goods is passive, and advocating existing domestic goods is also passive. If we can combine the non-existent and strive to manufacture it, then that is our active method. If we implement this method, the necessary condition is to study Japan. What special things does Japan use to invade us most every year? In this way, we can have a basis. As far as the brothers know, it can be divided into four types: (1) Goods imported from customs: From 1929, the goods that exceeded 10 million at customs were sugar, cotton paper, flour, coal, and fish. It is lamentable to say that coal and sugar are still produced in Taiwan and the Northeast! (2) Japanese industrial raw materials exported: We know that there are wool, soybean cake, iron sand, etc. (3) Japanese factories in Shanghai and the three northeastern provinces: According to a recent survey, there are 43 factories with 1,064,206,84 spinning machines and 1,5467 wire machines. Their aggressive businesses also include ironwork, ceramics, brewing, transportation, printing, finance, rubber, and general merchandise industries, etc. (4) Tariff issues: In name, China is autonomous, but in reality, China is suffering. Now I am also thinking about Japan's research on us. It is really terrible to say that they are helping us research everything that we have inherent and have not taken care of. I remember that on the first page of the 30th anniversary album of the Xujiahui Tongwen College years ago, there was my map with many red lines drawn on it. It is said that the red lines indicate the routes that have been investigated and researched. Everyone, think back to how we are, how many people can do it in person? I often blame the warning words "Beware of Pickpockets" posted on the market. Our treasures are being picked off by others every day, why don't we know how to prevent them? Alas, the Japanese are really powerful. In the 60 years since the Restoration, they did not have the ability to accept Western culture at first and still used translations from Chinese. Now we have to learn everything from him. If you look at literature, medicine, philosophy, and science, how many are translated from them? No wonder Mr. Ma Xiangbo said, "Japan has jumped from eight to five among the world's eight great powers, and now it has jumped from five to one." Finally, I have two words for everyone. Our problem is like a suitcase that is lost and found. One person is looking for things in the box but can't remember clearly. One person said how many clothes and books are in my box, and how much money is there. As a result, who should get it? It's like a rich person buys an expensive book and ignores it, while a poor person steals a look at this expensive book. Who gets the result in reality? Gentlemen, China is this suitcase and this book.

Local News Two

Two People Drown While Swimming 84

A Chinese man... a Russian child

The "North China Daily News" reports that on Sunday, a man named Sheng Delin (transliteration) drowned while swimming in an open-air swimming pool on Jiangwan Road. Initially, he sank to the bottom of the pool unnoticed. After the pool's rescue team searched for about an hour, they finally found him. Mr. Sheng and a relative entered the pool at 11:30 AM, floating and swimming for a while. Suddenly, around 12:00 PM, Mr. Sheng was nowhere to be found. His relative searched back and forth without success and urgently reported it to Mr. Gulang, a Westerner at the ticket office, who summoned the on-duty rescue team to search the pool. It was not until 1:15 PM that they found the body lying face down at the bottom of five feet of water. After carrying him out, a doctor who happened to be at the pool examined him and determined that he had been dead for an hour and could not be saved. The fire department was notified to transport him to the Red Cross Hospital on Haig Road in an ambulance. Mr. Sheng was 32 years old and had only been in Shanghai for a week because his sister was working as a nurse at the Red Cross Hospital, so he was temporarily staying there.

Also, on Saturday afternoon, a Russian child named Xie Leifu drowned while swimming in the Minhang Pujiang River with two friends. His body has not yet been recovered. Xie is known to have had heart problems, and it is believed that he had an attack that led to his drowning.

Japanese Residents in Shanghai Elect "Miss Shanghai" 85

Takeko Inoue Officially Elected, Previously Awarded "Miss Japan" Title

The Japanese "Shanghai Nichi Nichi Shimbun," published in this city, organized an election for "Miss Shanghai" among Japanese residents in Shanghai. About two hundred contestants participated, including young ladies, students, store clerks, geishas, and dancers. Readers cast public votes, and the ten candidates with the most votes in the previous week were chosen as the official candidates for "Miss Shanghai." Then, the newspaper hired ten respected judges to impartially examine the ten candidates based on their health and beauty to select "Miss Shanghai." Yesterday, the newspaper published the results of the judging.

A Small Portrait of Takeko Inoue 86

Takeko Inoue was selected as the first-place winner, "Miss Shanghai" for Japanese residents in Shanghai. The second-place winner was Junko Osumi, and the third-place winner was Toshiko Toyama. Takeko Inoue is currently twenty years old, skilled in embroidery and sports, and recently became the secretary to the Reverend Kozui Otani. Otani was the abbot of the Nishi Honganji Temple in Japan and is a member of the Japanese aristocracy. In June of this year, Inoue accompanied Otani on an inspection tour of Java and other regions in the South Seas, and she is scheduled to return to Shanghai in early September. Miss Inoue was recommended by the Dentsu agency and selected as "Miss Japan" this year. Now, she has happily won the title of "Miss Shanghai," which is an extraordinary honor. The second-place winner, Junko Osumi, is 21 years old and currently works as a typist at the Shanghai office of the Hanyeping Coal Mining Company. The third-place winner, Toshiko Toyama, is 24 years old and works as a dancer at the Qingniao Dance Hall.

Qinglian Pavilion Owner Accused of Assault by Concubine 87

Witness Zhu Lingdi Testifies to the Defendant's Violent Actions

Sun Yunqing (also known as Shao Rui), the 65-year-old owner of the Qinglian Pavilion teahouse on Fuzhou Road from Shanxi Province, was recently sued by his fourth concubine, Jiang Cuiling, through lawyer Chen Bingsing at the First Special District Court for assault and other charges. The court summoned him for questioning on the 10th of this month, and the details were recorded in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Shen Shumu continued the hearing, with many men and women in attendance. The plaintiff Jiang Cuiling's lawyer, Chen Bingsing, and the defendant Sun Yunqing's lawyers, Zhang Deqin and Ni Zheng'ao, were also present on time. The plaintiff, Jiang Cuiling, with a delicate face, wearing a lake-blue printed Indian silk cheongsam, flesh-colored stockings, and gauze shoes, arrived hurriedly at the start of the trial. Judge Shen then questioned Ms. Jiang, who stated that she was 26 years old, from Haimen, and lived on North Chengdu Road. (Question) What is your relationship with the defendant? (Answer) I am the defendant's fourth concubine. (Question) How old were you when you became a concubine? (Answer) Fifteen years old. The defendant's treatment of me has always been poor. (Question) What are you accusing him of now? (Answer) I am accusing him of abuse and assault. (Question) When and what time? (Answer) Noon on July 22nd. (Question) What caused the assault? (Answer) Because on the night of July 21st, the defendant forcibly wanted to share a room with me, and I refused. The next day, I was slapped twice and punched in the chest, causing me to be injured and cough up blood. (Question) Were there any witnesses at the time? (Answer) Yes, Lingdi saw it. At this point, her lawyer, Chen, presented the prescription of the Chinese medicine practitioner Wang Zhongqi who treated Ms. Jiang and elaborated on the main points of the lawsuit on her behalf (the content of which was recorded in this newspaper on the 11th). He also stated that Ms. Jiang was also assaulted by the defendant in April of last year. There was a witness at the time, but she is now being held in confinement and is not allowed to testify. Furthermore, the witness, a woman named Zhu Lingdi, testified that she was 24 years old, lived on Shanhai Pass Road, and the defendant was her uncle, while the plaintiff was the defendant's fourth concubine. On July 22nd, when the defendant was beating the plaintiff in the room, she was also present and witnessed it. Then, the defendant's lawyer, Zhang Deqin, cross-examined Ms. Zhu once, and the defendant's testimony was full of evasions, claiming that the plaintiff's statements were entirely false. Why would I, at such an old age, beat her? As for the witness Zhu Lingdi, she only came to my house on July 24th, my father's birthday. How could she have seen it? However, after the plaintiff left, I received a letter from her lawyer, Chen, proposing conditions for divorce, including a request for me to deposit 20,000 yuan in the bank and provide the plaintiff with 200 yuan per month for living expenses and build a residence, etc. I did not agree, which led to this lawsuit. However, I have always treated the plaintiff well. We have lived together for over ten years and I have never abused her. She is suing me now, I believe, because she dislikes my old age. Judge Shen verified the statements and announced that the case would be adjourned to Wednesday for further hearing.

Guangdong Merchants' Hospital Resolves to Change Name 88

Investigation into Impersonation and Fundraising

The Guangdong Merchants' Hospital was originally established by Guangdong merchants in Shanghai. The hospital's board of directors felt that the term "Guangdong Merchants" was too narrow in scope, and the annual expenses have been supported by donations from various sectors of the Guangdong community in Shanghai, not just by Guangdong merchants' capital. Therefore, it was resolved to change the name to Guangdong Hospital to better reflect the situation. The hospital's board of directors, in accordance with the regulations, convened a temporary meeting of founders and donors yesterday to legally resolve the name change to Guangdong Hospital, effective January 1st of next year. However, recently, unscrupulous individuals have been impersonating the Guangdong Hospital to solicit donations from Chinese and foreign individuals. Yesterday, the Changxing Shipping Company at No. 1 Guangdong Road and others brought receipts to the hospital for inquiry and found out they had been deceived. It was discovered that the hospital has been established for nine years, and all expenses have been covered by donations from the hospital's staff. Any Guangdong people who are enthusiastic about donating also send their donations to the hospital and receive receipts. The hospital has never sent personnel to solicit donations from the outside world. An investigation into the impersonation is currently underway.

Renovation of Central District Telephone Nearly Complete 89

Expected to Return to Normal Today

Mr. Baode, the general manager of Shanghai Telephone Company, stated in an interview with a reporter from the Shenshi Telegraph Agency that the conversion of the central district's automatic telephone exchange to a fully automated system has been actively underway in recent days. However, during the conversion, the central district's automatic telephone exchange inevitably experienced congestion, making it difficult for telephones starting with the number "1" to connect or temporarily unable to connect. This is not due to telephone damage but is an unavoidable difficulty during the conversion process, similar to how congestion on a railway requires the preceding train to move before the following train can proceed. Therefore, the company published a notice on the 17th, advising central district users to refrain from using non-emergency telephones for the time being to reduce difficulties. The company is also working hard to minimize inconvenience to users. The renovation is expected to be completed today, and normal service should be restored.

A Mediator Loses His Life 96

Zhu Monk Dies with Eyes Unclosed

Huang Pi Asan, a rogue living upstairs in a carpenter shop at No. 278 Rue Massenet in the French Concession, approached Jiang Jinshan, a clerk, at the Xinfuyuan Teahouse No. 153 Xujiahui Road on the 13th to borrow five yuan, and when he did not succeed, the two sides started an argument. Zhu Monk (age 46, resident of No. 10 Ronghua Lane, Rue Massenet), a barber from Changshu in the teahouse, stepped forward to mediate. Afterwards, Huang, displeased with Zhu's mediation, gathered three or four people with wooden sticks and axes to confront Zhu on the afternoon of the 14th. They attacked him with sticks and axes, causing Zhu's legs to be slashed ten times, and he fell to the ground with stick injuries. The perpetrators fled immediately. Then, the teahouse attendant, A Mao, notified Zhu's wife, Fu, who reported it to the police. Zhu was taken to Guangci Hospital, where he died from his injuries on the afternoon of the 16th. The hospital notified the police station to send a detective to take the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch for an autopsy. Yesterday, the police chief reported to the Second Special Court, and Prosecutor Ding Shikui, along with forensic doctor Wei Ligong and clerk Zhao Yifen, arrived at the scene at 3:00 PM to perform the autopsy and take notes. According to the deceased's wife, Zhu Fu, her husband was hacked to death. Mr. Ding verified the statement and determined that Zhu Monk had indeed died from injuries inflicted by an ax and sticks. The body was released to the deceased's wife for burial, pending the police's arrest of the perpetrators.

Interrogation of the Hotel Assassination Case 97

The Fa Shang Xin Hotel at No. 113 Rue des Sœurs in the French Concession experienced a vendetta case in Room 2 around 7:00 PM on the 15th, injuring Zhong Zhiqing and Chen Yiming, and killing Xia Yongsheng and a Mr. Xue. After a special operation by the French police the next day, the suspects Yan Er, Yan Li, and Dai Yunhong, all from Jiangbei, were apprehended and taken to the police station for investigation. The details were reported in yesterday's newspaper. Now, it is known that Yan Er, also known as Jin Biao, is 31 years old and from Funing. Li (actually Zhang), 19, is Yan's mistress. Dai is Yan's cousin. Yesterday, the police escorted them to the Second Special Court. Judge Xiong Huihua and Prosecutor Lou Guangguang presided over the criminal court and questioned them. First, the police lawyer, Fei Xizhen, presented the case and requested an adjournment so that the police could conduct a detailed investigation and arrest the accomplices. Yan testified under his real name, Jin Biao, and denied that he was Yan Er. He claimed to be a boatman and denied any involvement in the vendetta case. Zhang testified that she had been Yan's mistress for only two months and knew nothing about the murder. Dai testified that he worked as a rickshaw puller and was arrested for asking Yan for a loan. He denied any knowledge of the vendetta case. Judge Xiong verified the statements and questioned Wang Jiemei, the manager of the Fa Shang Xin Hotel, and Zhang Rongsheng, the tea boy, about the circumstances of the incident. Then, he ordered the defendants to be remanded in custody and granted an adjournment for further questioning.

Thief Killed After Crying Out for Capture 98

Zhang Boyin Dies Tragically

At around 9:00 AM yesterday, three robbers suddenly appeared at the Yongmao Rice Store on Rue Amiral Courbet north of Avenue Joffre. One robber stood guard outside, while two robbers went inside. One robber used a gun to threaten the store clerk while standing on the counter, while the other robber went inside to steal only 20 yuan from the drawer of the accounting table. When the police from the Liyuan Road police station of the Second District arrived, the robbers were long gone. They ordered Gu Zhongli, the local representative of the 15th District, to report the case to the local court for an autopsy. Incoming Mail

The Nature and Purpose of the Pacific International Studies Association (Continued) by Chen Liting 111

The establishment and work of the Pacific International Studies Association have already been briefly described above. The fourth conference will be held in our country in October of this year, and the time is approaching. Recently, there have been many misunderstandings from the outside world and a lack of deep understanding. Therefore, I will specifically elaborate on its nature and purpose. Subsequently, I will continue to write about its organization, work, and the process of the previous three conferences, and discuss the content of this conference to clarify the truth, dispel misunderstandings, and resolve doubts.

The nature of the Pacific International Studies Association can be seen from its constituent members. During the first conference, its members were mainly from the YMCA, similar to an international conference of religious activists. However, since the second conference, the composition of the members has been quite different from the past. It includes diplomats, educators, politicians, scholars, doctors, lawyers, entrepreneurs, and religious figures, with religious figures being a minority. It is not similar to the initial stage, which had religious connotations. Its members are neither entrusted by the governments of various countries nor representatives of groups with specific interests. They participate purely in a private capacity. Therefore, its nature is also different from political or economic conferences between countries. During discussions, they can speak freely and frankly, expressing themselves completely. After completion, there are not only no resolutions to be made, but also no need to seek consensus or express any particular position. The goal is to use research and discussion methods to reveal the crux of each issue and the cultural and socio-economic situation of each country to the world, and solutions will naturally emerge. This is also different from other conferences that require a formal meeting structure and specific results. In summary, the nature of the Pacific International Studies Association is simply the organization of an international private academic group.

Since this association is an organization of private groups, its purpose is completely different from various international organizations with formal missions. I will briefly list them as follows: (1) Appointing specialists to be responsible for on-site research to use the results of this research to stimulate continuous research on other Pacific issues. (2) The results of the research, whether in the form of papers or reports, are printed and exchanged with each other. When they are mature, they are used as the basis for discussing various issues. (3) Although it is impossible to obtain resolutions after discussion, the process of this discussion and the research of various experts can be published to the world, allowing the general reader to understand the content of the issue, so that correct public opinion can be generated. Moreover, because there is no resolution format, discussions are more detailed and unrestricted. (4) With clear and detailed research on facts, issues between various countries and ethnic groups can be used to promote mutual understanding.

The above is about its nature and purpose. I have often lamented that people in our country are indifferent to the changes in the global situation and the state of international politics and economics. Even the important issues within the country, such as how much industry is treasured, and other important political and economic issues, are mostly unknown except for a few who know the general outline. Therefore, in the past few decades, whenever there have been major domestic and foreign affairs, we have always suffered from a lack of reliable information to determine the direction of solutions. Doing things rashly often leads to delays and missed opportunities. Moreover, many important issues in our country are related to foreign countries. Due to the lack of publicity, the true facts are not clear to the world, which leads other foreigners to be confused by one-sided arguments and unable to have a correct public opinion. The facts are there, and everyone in the country is familiar with them. Now there is an international academic organization, the Pacific International Studies Association, which uses research as the basis for discussing various issues. The participation of people from the industrial and academic circles of various countries will inevitably reveal their difficulties and the results of their research directly, so that foreigners can understand the true situation. Although there is no solution to be found, the opinions disclosed by these experts may suggest possible policies for the governments of various countries. According to the second conference, British and Chinese representatives exchanged ideas frankly, and British policy was subsequently improved. At the third conference in Kyoto, a fierce debate on the issue of the three northeastern provinces awakened the Japanese people from the delusion that Dalian was already in their possession. In practice, this type of organization is not only sufficient to promote our people's understanding of the situation abroad, but also to enable foreigners to understand the current situation of our society, economy, and culture, as well as various important issues related to foreign countries. It is truly beneficial and harmless, and there seems to be no reason to criticize it.

The fourth Pacific International Studies Association conference was invited by our country's representatives to be held in China when the third conference was convened in Kyoto, Japan in 1929. Recently, active preparations have been made in various aspects. The content of this conference is divided into major and specialized categories. The major categories are (1) the international economic relations of the Pacific Ocean, and (2) China's international relations. The specialized categories are (1) food and population issues, (2) the political, social, and economic problems of non-independent ethnic groups in the Pacific Ocean, (3) cultural issues, (4) immigration and ethnic issues, and (5) labor issues and living standards. The topics discussed are the main issues in the Pacific Ocean today. Gathering specialized talents from various countries in one place to discuss related issues in detail will provide choices for those who solve these problems in the future. The purpose is clear and not to be criticized. Moreover, according to the Prime Minister's theory, it is not difficult to implement, but difficult to know. Today, China's economic and social problems are as numerous as hemp. Those who can thoroughly study and understand the crux of the problem are very few. The results of the discussions on various issues in our country at this conference will surely provide resources for reflection. The assistance from other mountains can be used, so how can it be said that it is not helpful?

Words of Wisdom 112

— Man Yin

Success or failure in a career is not enough to judge a hero. Beauty or ugliness of appearance is not enough to measure a beauty.

Those who encounter many difficulties in doing things gain practical experience. Those who experience turbulence in love see true love.

Being in the world is like crossing a river. One should be careful when encountering strong winds and huge waves. Even when the wind is calm and the waves are calm, one should be diligent.

It is better to strive for life in reality than to seek pleasure in dreams.

Love without conditions is a lie. Affection with a cause is a proper statement.

If people can measure the hearts of others with their own hearts, then many unnecessary disputes in society can be reduced.

Young men and women can gain a lot of unexpected intelligence when seeking love, but they add a lot of unnecessary troubles when heartbroken.

The world in dreams is, after all, mirages. The world after waking up is the real world.

Love is like war. A beautiful face is a tactic. A glorious position is a soldier. Money is the food, weapons, and ammunition. If the tactics are not clever and the soldiers are not numerous, it is not enough to defeat the enemy. If the food is not plentiful and the weapons are not sophisticated, it is even less sufficient to win.

In modern agencies or companies, there is a kind of extremely unequal fact. That is, those who do more work receive less pay, and those who do less work receive more pay.

Peace comes from struggle. Justice is determined by power.

The twentieth century is a world where people eat people. Whoever has the qualifications to eat, also has the qualifications to be eaten.

The Rising and Non-Receding Capital Flood 113

— Jiguan

The capital's flood disaster has been repeatedly reported by newspapers. In the past ten days, although the weather has been sunny and hot, the waterside area has not only not receded, but has also gradually risen. According to the people of the capital, the river water will not go ashore. Once it goes ashore, it cannot recede for several weeks. Now the water is accumulated on the flat ground, and the water depth can submerge the thighs. Even the footboards of rickshaws are submerged. If it rises a foot or so, traffic in the city will inevitably be blocked. This is probably because the upstream areas such as Hankou and Jiujiang are vast oceans that flood downstream, so the capital's river flow rises without receding.

I once saw in Shanghai newspapers that during the continuous rain in the capital, the streets and alleys were mostly turned into wetlands, and the ponds on both sides of Zhongshan Road overflowed. The fish scattered, so some set nets on the road to catch them. This is not the capital of the present great flood. Not only the fish on the road have escaped, but also the river water is turbulent, and fishing boats dare not take risks. It is not easy to catch, and the price has increased. The fish and shrimp on the market have been sold at more than double the usual price.

There is one more thing that those who do not understand the situation in the capital will inevitably find strange when they hear it. The residents of the capital mostly take water from the well. Drinking water comes from the river bank. All are carried by coolies who use waterwheels to move. Now the river water is several feet deep, and the streets of Xiaguan are mostly flooded. If you take water in the street, you can see cars and horses coming and going, and bare feet running in the water. It is dirty and unclean, and it is difficult to fill drinks. As for transportation on the riverside, it is unusually difficult to drag because of the deep water and heavy load. Affected by this, the source of drinking water is gradually becoming scarce. As a result, several public bathhouses have raised water prices. In the past, one copper coin per spoonful is now increased to three times. At this time, the weather is still hot and there is more demand for water, so everyone is frowning. The flood is due to excessive water, but unexpectedly, the drinking water has become a strange commodity due to the accumulation of water on the streets. This can also be said to be a strange thing.

Small Recipes 114

— Yang Yixiao

Garlic Tofu: Cut the new garlic sprouts into minced pieces. Add small cubes of tofu to the pot, add a little shrimp, and cook for one minute. It is exceptionally fresh and tender.

Red Water Chestnut Cake: Peel the red water chestnut, cut into thin slices. Mix with lotus root powder, agar-agar, peppermint, and white sugar. Stir well and cook for one minute. Take it out and wait for it to cool. It will congeal into a cake.

Chestnut Crisp: Peel the chestnuts. Stew until they are soft and cooked. Then use dry noodles, add lard and stir-fry. Mix well. Add a little white sugar and assorted dried fruits. Knead into a crisp. It is exceptionally soft.

Sugar Lotus Root Porridge: Take lotus root and fill it with glutinous rice. Put it in a pot with a glutinous rice bag and cook with brown sugar to make porridge. It is fragrant, sweet, and delicious.

Dried Longan Balls: Take fresh dried longan. Remove the shell and pit. Season with noodles and put it in a hot oil pan. Fry until both sides are golden brown. It is extremely delicious.

Rock as Described by His Loving Mother 115

— Mo Yi

Rock grew up in California, USA. When I (Rock's mother claims the following) discovered his theatrical talent, there was no such thing as movies. So I wanted to make him a famous stage actor. And he himself decided to go down this road. But I didn't expect him to have today. Although his success is due to his theatrical talent, it is ultimately attributed to "movies." If he were a stage actor, I am afraid he would not be famous in the world.

When he was very young, he and his brother, Gerald, performed some childish games. In their view, it was a dramatic act. But sometimes I felt they were quite interesting. So I gave them some guidance. When he grew up a little and went to school, he already had considerable achievements. His performance was simply not childish at all. In school, he often participated in talent shows and performed comedies, which won him good reputation. People praised him as a promising comedian.

When he was sixteen years old, his father took him to see a movie he had never seen before. This was terrible. Since watching the movie, it was simply difficult to stay at home. He was always outside all day long. I don't know what he was doing outside. Soon, the news that he went to a movie company to work as an extra reached my ears.

One day, the director chose him from a large group of children and asked him to try it. He performed very well and was able to satisfy the director. So his name was entered in the payroll. But his talent was not discovered by the director. He only played a supporting role. He played all supporting roles. And he could play them vividly. The audience said that he had a bright future.

He has a picky temper. So he has never been satisfied with the movies he starred in. He always wanted to have better results next time. If someone praised him for his good performance in person, he would always answer, "I don't think so. You think this movie performed well here or there. But I still don't think it's so good. I think I might have more satisfactory results next time."

Although he is famous all over the world now, he is still a simple-minded, enthusiastic worker, and a completely childish person. He loves sports. The house has a fifteen-acre sports field. Among them, there is a nine-hole miniature golf course, tennis and baseball fields, and a large swimming pool. He is as dedicated to sports as he is to filming. So he has a very strong physique. He neither smokes nor drinks. What is even more strange is that he doesn't even like tea and coffee. He only likes to drink cold milk. His family is full of happy air. His love for his wife is unmatched in the world. And he loves his two daughters, one son, and loves his wife as much as he loves her.

A Short Account of the Farewell Party for Students Going Abroad 116

— Ping

Yesterday, various cultural groups at sea held a farewell party for this year's students going abroad at the Chen Family Garden on Seymour Road. More than 150 guests attended. The garden is grand and spacious. We enjoyed, strolled, and chatted in the thick shade of green trees, which was already full of leisure and fun. In addition, there were photography, tea parties, speeches, music, and so on. Naturally, there were many materials to record. So I extracted one or two to make people smile.

The Little Sisters Also Swim: The facilities of Chen's Garden are really good. There are sports fields and family swimming pools. Their whole family, old and young, all like sports very much. Before the meeting started, we watched swimming around the pool. There were four little sisters who were the granddaughters of the garden owner, Chen Bingqian. The youngest was five or six years old, and the oldest was only twelve or three years old. They floated and sank freely in the clear waves. They were very familiar with various swimming styles. And they can jump into the water from a very high diving board. It can be seen from the glimpse of their training. This kind of family sports is worth imitating by our people.

Xu Peihuang's Sincere Heart: After the scene of taking pictures on the lawn was over, we entered the auditorium in order. Among the guests were educators, scientists, diplomats, economists, and socialites. They were all together. The ages ranged from ten years old to seventy or eighty years old. The so-called "the wise and the young gathered together." This meeting seemed similar. Chairman Xu Peihuang gave a speech after the ceremony. He started by saying "...recalling the students who went abroad in 1909, they had to cut off their braids first and put on a Western suit. But no one would come to say goodbye. Only you send yourself. The family members cried and said goodbye reluctantly. However, it was only twenty years ago. It's really too far apart. He hopes that students studying abroad will carefully observe the essence of European and American material civilization, and the spirit of seeking truth from facts and marching forward bravely, and bring them back to the motherland for application. If you learn their extravagant habits, such as the splendor of the dance halls, and compare the advantages and disadvantages of the Shanghai Da Dong and Da Hu, then you will go on the wrong path."

Wu Jingxiong's Overseas Romance: Some people call Mr. Wu a foreign doctor. But this time his great theory praised the prosperity of poetry, books, etiquette, music, and ancient Chinese academics. He said, "For example, the news industry and public opinion authority in Europe and the United States have only recently become great. In China, Confucius and the ancient masters revised the Book of Poetry and compiled the Spring and Autumn Annals thousands of years ago. He was the original news reporter. Westerners' intelligence and talent cannot catch up with us Chinese. So don't be discouraged." He also said himself, "I am old and cannot do anything for the country. I hope you all will do well." In fact, Mr. Wu is only in his thirties, in his prime and promising. How can he be called old? Finally, he reported the anecdote in Europe and the United States earlier. "In a certain year in the United States, a general youth took perms as fashionable. I also often went to get perms. Unless I didn't have money by my side, I wanted to try dancing and prostitution. Especially those who went to Paris should avoid the temptation of lust. Once I saw a beautiful young girl in a theater in Paris. She gave me several loving hints and started her seduction work. I politely refused and said, "I am already married and cannot love you." She calmly replied. "It doesn't matter if you are married." It is not easy to deal with such a lewd society. Wu drew east and west, and his witty remarks were full of fun. He spoke in a Shanghai accent, mixed with Ningbo dialect, Mandarin, and English. The audience could not help but laugh.

Wu Zonglian's Interesting Words During the Meeting: A senior in the diplomatic circle, former Italian ambassador Wu Zonglian, also came with a cane. The old man was very interested and in good health. But he was deaf in both ears. In the quiet meeting place, he made a few loud and interesting remarks. When Wu Jingxiong gave a speech, he asked, "Who is it?" Someone wrote "Wu Jingxiong" in reply. He said, "Oh, he is Wu Jingxiong. He is so young, why does he say he is old?" He also said, "Mr. Wu's romance adds a lot of good materials to the newspaper." Because his voice was loud, the audience burst into laughter, breaking the silent air. Some people said that the old man heard very clearly and his ears were not bad.

Luo Chihui Said He Wanted to Be a Thief: The chairman announced that each person would add music to help the fun after the speech to meet the needs of the audience's psychology. Ms. Li Xianmin and Mrs. Guang Di's piano, Chen Zhijun's solo, and Mr. Dai Cuilun's harmonica were highly praised by the audience. The next student representatives gave a reply. Ms. Luo Chihui studied in Europe, and Mr. Lin Shibo studied in the United States. Ms. Luo said, "We must have the ability to be thieves and steal things when we go abroad." Some people thought, what is the intention of saying this immoral behavior? She continued, "In addition to working hard in books, we must use clever methods to steal the secret things in their science..." Everyone understood this extraordinary insight. The meeting ended at seven o'clock with great interest.

The Storytelling Rotary Club

Women Women (23) 117

— Yao Sufeng

After everything was made clear, Miss Ding realized that Mr. Lu was really a heartless liar. He lied to himself, his parents, his wife, and her. I only hate myself for not seeing clearly at the beginning, but relying on his temporary false flattery, I thought he was a good man to entrust my life to, so I suffered a lot of injustice. How can I not regret it?

Xiao Rong's wife heard Miss Ding tell her about the past, and she really felt sorry for Miss Ding. The two people talked and talked. Although they all complained about themselves, sighed sometimes, and shed tears sometimes, they talked very speculatively, and they did not hate each other at all.

"You have come to Shanghai alone and are unfamiliar. Stay here with me today. After a while, he will definitely come. Then question him!" Miss Ding immediately ordered Qiu Zi to arrange a bed for Xiao Rong's wife to live in, and instructed Qiu Zi not to tell the old lady, lest she get angry. But I thought about it myself, and I couldn't help but feel a burst of sadness.

At this time, it suddenly started raining heavily. In the lightning and thunder, the doorbell rang.

Qiu Zi was arranging the bedding upstairs. When he heard the doorbell ring, he opened the small window in front and saw that it was Mr. Lu who was back. He immediately ran downstairs to tell Miss Ding.

When Miss Ding heard Qiu Zi say that Mr. Lu was back, the fire in her heart burst out, but she thought that if he came in and exposed the matter, he would inevitably become angry and annoyed, and maybe he would cause trouble. It would be even more unpleasant to publicize it. Therefore, Miss Ding told Xiao Rong's wife to wait in her own room upstairs for a while, and repeatedly told her not to come out and quarrel with Xiao Rong immediately when she saw him, so as to act accordingly.

Xiao Rong's wife already believed in Miss Ding very much, so she listened to her and was led upstairs by Qiu Zi to hide in Miss Ding's back room. At the same time, Miss Ding went to open the door herself and let Xiao Rong in.

"Why didn't you open the door for so long? The rain is so heavy that my clothes are wet!" Mr. Lu said with a smile. Miss Ding did not answer him, but went upstairs by herself. Mr. Lu followed behind and went to the bedroom together.

Mr. Lu took off his clothes and sat down. He saw that Miss Ding's expression was not good, and she didn't say a word. He was naturally a little strange. He asked, "Why is your face so bad today? And you didn't say anything?"

"I'm sick," Miss Ding replied briefly.

"You have to see a doctor when you are sick!" Mr. Lu was still very attentive.

"I don't need to see a doctor. I think you should know the cause of my illness!" Miss Ding's voice trembled when she spoke.

Youth Zone

The Sound of the Qin 118

— Ke

Every day when the setting sun falls and the night falls, I hurry to collect the messy books and stand in front of the window on the street with a kind of quiet mood, looking at the changing clouds in the beautiful sunset. At this time, there will always be a familiar sound of the Huqin coming from the alley. When she plays the wandering and tragic tune and walks past my window, it will inevitably cause a vibration in my heart and send out a desolate feeling of being in a foreign land.

After a hot and stuffy day, white clouds gradually began to gather in the sky, becoming more and more numerous, and suddenly turning into a gray vault of heaven. The leaves of the drooping sycamore tree rustled in the wind. Dragonflies flew in groups around the shade of the trees. Under the trees, there was a noisy chatter of children laughing and adults talking. At this time, the intermittent sound of the Huqin drifted into the alley again, passed under the window, turned into the narrow alley behind the house, and suddenly turned back, stopping suddenly under the sycamore tree. It seemed that she had tightened the strings, and then played rhythmically, mixed with the woman's hoarse singing.

I sat at the table and looked down. "Ah!" There were so many people under the tree, adults and children, standing and sitting, in a circle. In the middle of the circle, there was a long bench with a woman in her forties sitting on it. Her hair was long and draped below her collar, her skin was yellow and thin, and her shoulders were high. She was playing the Huqin and opening and closing her wide lips, emitting a kind of broken bronze sound. Although her singing was so unpleasant and could not arouse people's pleasure, the people gathered around to listen all appeared so excited, so happy, so proud, especially the nanny of the Li family next door. She patted her fat belly and often patted the fat feet of a fat white child in her arms, her eyes smiling like Maitreya Buddha.

"Little sister, how old are you? Do you like to listen to songs?" After the woman finished singing, she leaned the Huqin on her body and pulled a girl standing in front of her and asked. The girl smiled and nodded, took out a few copper coins from her pocket and gave them to her.

"Oh, thank you, little sister. You are really sensible!" A kind of unnatural flattery appeared on her face full of wrinkles. She shrugged her shoulders and looked at everyone and said.

So a few people in them also gave her some money.

"Hey, how much money can you earn every day like this?" A woman wearing glasses and sewing clothes asked.

"Alas, sometimes I can't even get a bowl of white rice," she twisted her neck and sighed slightly.

Member of the Sea Star Troupe, Yu Yan 119

— (Photo by Bing)

"Then why did you do that? Aren't things like what we do more reliable?" Aunt Zhang from my house said with pity.

"Yes, but who would want to hire me? I am so weak," she said, rubbing her eyes with a handkerchief, making the rims of her eyes red. "There is nothing I can do now, I am always short of breath and coughing – there were good days before, but now there is nothing left, just a beggar on the street."

"There were good days before? What was that like?" everyone asked in surprise, as if this was an interesting story. She glanced at them, hesitated slightly, and frowned, saying, "Speaking of which... " She contradicted herself, "But what does it matter? Who can control their own destiny when they are young?" She then began to tell her story, saying,

"When I was eight years old, there was a famine in my hometown. My parents, unable to endure the hunger day and night, took

Page 20

me to Jiangnan. At that time, I was so surprised and envious of the prosperity and beauty I had never seen before. I didn't know anything, just followed my parents wandering the streets and alleys all day long. Once, a sneaky-looking stranger said something to my father and forcibly dragged me to a place. I seemed to know that it was not good for me, and I kept crying – my mother seemed to be shedding tears too – but it was all useless. Finally, he sent me to someone's house."

"Oh, was it a mansion? Was it a house of prostitution?" Li's nanny asked.

"Guess," she smiled and continued.

"I spent two or three years in a daze, and then someone introduced me to a theater to live the life of an opera singer – I played a female martial role."

"That's not easy, can you do those tricks?" A cook-like man standing at the base of the wall said.

"Yes, I've liked doing these things since I was little."

"Who taught you?" Li's nanny said.

"No one taught me, I learned it playing with the children next door."

"Have some virtue, always interrupting people," the woman wearing glasses said impatiently.

She touched her hair and continued,

"One day, which was the last day of my luck, was a night of bright lights and fancy drinks. I was drinking and playing finger-guessing games with gentlemen in a beautiful hotel. At that time, because I had had a few more drinks, I walked out of the hotel door in a daze and took a car straight to the theater. That night, the opera I was performing required me to somersault down from three stacked tables with two tea tables stacked on top. I went on stage and performed a few sets of sword and spear routines. Although I felt a little dizzy and lightheaded, I finally climbed to the highest point as usual, supported my waist with both hands, and bent my head backwards... In that instant, I immediately realized my danger. Everything went dark, my head felt heavy, and with a sudden loud noise, countless sparks flashed before my eyes, and then I knew nothing."

"I woke up in a hospital. When I opened my eyes, I immediately saw that everything had changed, it was so blurry and dark. When I realized that I had become disabled – I had broken an eyeball – I was so sad and cried... I wished I could die immediately. I understood that my appearance was ruined, and my life was also extinguished."

"Alas," she sighed deeply. "I walked out of the hospital with only one eye, and no one recognized me anymore. My fate was decided in this way, to wander and sing on the streets forever."

"Alas, so pitiful," everyone sighed.

She sat silently for a while, then lazily stood up and yawned.

At this moment, her face was facing my window, and suddenly I saw a white eyeball with a network of blood vessels protruding from below her right eyebrow, appearing extremely frightening.

She slowly picked up her erhu, touched her hair again, said "Goodbye" to everyone, and then walked out of the alley, playing a meandering tune.

Initiator of the Sea Star Troupe, Ms. Tao Chun 120

— (Photo by Bing)

Guidelines for Submissions to the Youth Garden 121

(1) The text should focus on discussions about youth issues, news about domestic and foreign schools or students, essays, descriptions of school life, and personal notes. The style is not limited.

(2) Pictures should be limited to those related to youth issues.

(3) Photos that qualify should be related to youth life (such as sports, travel, excursions, theatrical performances, gatherings, exhibitions, various competitions, etc.), school news, and youth movements. Both individuals and groups are welcome. Do not write two words on manuscript paper.

(4) Each text should not exceed two thousand words.

(5) Write horizontally, do not write carelessly. Western text can be omitted if possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

Whether or not a manuscript is published, it will not be returned. If you need it returned,

(6) Do not write horizontally, do not write carelessly. Western text can be omitted if possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(7) Do not use water for drawings, do not use colored paper, use white paper and black drawings.

(8) Send submissions to the Editorial Department of Youth Garden.
